Consequences of Ila': Expiation and Bain Divorce
Rulings on expiation and bain divorce from Ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on expiation and divorce upon breaking or completing the Ila' period, and apply the rules regarding claims of intercourse.

Core Idea
Intercourse during Ila' requires expiation; no intercourse after four months triggers bain divorce.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq details the legal consequences of Ila' (a vow to abstain from marital intercourse). It clarifies when expiation is obligatory, when a bain divorce occurs, and how claims of intercourse are handled procedurally. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly applying the law of Ila'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage first addresses the case where the husband has intercourse during the four-month period, then the case where he does not. Identify each scenario and its ruling.
Intercourse → expiation; no intercourse → bain divorce.
2
Understand the expiation requirement
Note that expiation is only required if the oath was by Allah. Also, expiation before intercourse is invalid. Consider the distinction between worldly obligation and otherworldly forgiveness.
The three Imams agree on this.
3
Analyze the bain divorce ruling
Why is the divorce bain (irrevocable) rather than revocable? Because it prevents the husband from taking her back and resuming the injustice. The iddah begins at the time of separation, not at the pronouncement.
Based on reports from several Companions.
4
Examine the evidentiary rules
If the husband claims intercourse within the four months, his word is accepted. After the period, his word is not accepted, but he may prove it with evidence (beyond reasonable doubt). Understand the principle behind this.
Mansur's confession is trusted because he could have done it.
5
Differentiate oath duration
If he swore for four months, the oath drops automatically after that period. If he swore indefinitely or forever, the oath remains and the Ila' continues.
This affects whether future actions require new expiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن وطئ في المدة كفّر بتشديد الفاء أي لزمته الكفارة إذا كانت يمينه بالله تعالى وبه قالت الأئمة الثلاثة ووعد المغفرة بسبب الفيء الذي هو مثل التوبة لا ينافي الزام الكفارة لأنه حكم دنيوي وذاك أخروي. قيد بالوطء لأنه لو كفر قبله لا يكون كفارة؛ كذا ذكر الأسبيجابي. وأطلق في الوطء فشمل ما إذا جن بعد الإيلاء ثم وطئها انحلت وسقط الإيلاء ؛ كذا في فتح القدير قوله : وسقط الإيلاء بإجماع الفقهاء حتى لو مضت أربعة أشهر يقع طلاق لانحلال اليمين بالحنث وسواء حلف على أربعة أشهر أو أطلق أو على الأبد قوله : (وإلا بانت أي إن لم يطأ في المدة وهي أربعة أشهر وقعت عليه طلقة بائنة لأنه قد وقع التخلص من الظلم ولا يكون بالرجعي أن لأنه بسبيل من يردها إلى عصمته ويعبد الإيلاء فتعين البائن لتملك نفسها وتزول سلطنته عنها جزاء لظلمه وهو مروي عن عثمان بن عفان وزيد بن ثابت وعلي وابن مسعود وابن عباس وابن عمر رضي الله عنهم وتمامه في فتح القدير. وذكر الأسبيجابي أن العدة من وقت البينونة وبه فارق الطلاق الرجعي فإنه وإن أوجب بينونة في ثاني الحال كالإيلاء لكن العدة فيه من وقت الطلاق لا البينونة. وفي المبسوط : وإذا ادعى أنه قد جامعها فإن ادعى في الأربعة الأشهر فالقول قوله، وإن ادعى ذلك بعد مضي المدة لم يقبل قوله بناء على الأصل المعروف أنه متى أقر بما يملك انشاءه لا يكون متهماً، فلو أقام بينة على مقالته في الأربعة الأشهر أنه قد جامعها فهي امرأته لأن الثابت بإقراره كالثابت بالمعاينة وهي من أعجب المسائل أنه لا يقبل إقراره بعد مضي المدة ويتمكن من إثباته بالبينة ا هـ . قوله : (وسقط اليمين لو حلف على أربعة أشهر) لأنها موقتة بوقت فلا تبقى بعد مضيه قوله : ( وبقيت لو على الأبد أي بقيت اليمين لو كان حلف على الأبد سواء صرح به أو أطلق
His saying: (If he has intercourse during the period, he must expiate) — i.e., expiation becomes obligatory if his oath was by Allah Almighty, and upon this said the three Imams. And the promise of forgiveness due to the 'fay'' (return) which is like repentance does not negate the obligation of expiation because it is a worldly ruling and that is otherworldly. He restricted to intercourse because if he expiates before, it is not an expiation; thus mentioned al-Asbijabi. And he made absolute regarding intercourse, so it includes if he becomes insane after Ila' then has intercourse, it is dissolved and Ila' drops; thus in Fath al-Qadir. His saying: And the Ila' drops by consensus of the jurists, so if four months pass, divorce occurs due to the dissolution of the oath by breaking it, whether he swore for four months or absolutely or forever. His saying: (And otherwise she becomes separated) — i.e., if he does not have intercourse during the period of four months, a bain divorce occurs because relief from injustice has occurred, and it is not revocable because he is in a position to bring her back to his authority and resume Ila', so bain is determined so that she owns herself and his authority over her ends as a punishment for his injustice. This is narrated from Uthman ibn Affan, Zayd ibn Thabit, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them all). And al-Asbijabi mentioned that the iddah is from the time of bainuna, and by this it differs from revocable divorce, for even though it causes bainuna in the second instance like Ila', the iddah therein is from the time of divorce, not bainuna. And in al-Mabsut: And if he claims that he had intercourse with her, then if he claims during the four months, his word is accepted; if he claims after the period has passed, his word is not accepted based on the known principle that when one confesses to something he can create, he is not accused. So if he brings evidence for his statement during the four months that he had intercourse, she is his wife because what is established by his confession is like what is established by direct observation. And it is one of the most wondrous issues that his confession is not accepted after the period passes, but he can prove it by evidence. His saying: (And the oath drops if he swore for four months) because it is time-limited, so it does not remain after its passing. His saying: (And it remains if [he swore] for perpetuity) — i.e., the oath remains if he swore for perpetuity, whether he explicitly said so or it was absolute.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof covering several consequences of Ila'. First: if the husband has intercourse during the four-month period, he must perform expiation (kaffarah) provided his oath was by Allah. This is the ruling of the three Imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). The expiation is a worldly obligation; forgiveness for breaking the oath is a separate matter. Expiating before intercourse is invalid. If he becomes insane and then has intercourse, the Ila' drops. Second: if he does not have intercourse within four months, a single bain divorce occurs. This is based on the reports of several Companions. The divorce is bain (irrevocable) so that he cannot take her back and continue the Ila', which would be unjust. The iddah (waiting period) for the woman begins from the time of bainuna (separation), unlike revocable divorce where iddah starts from the pronouncement of divorce. Third: if the husband claims to have had intercourse within the four months, his word is accepted because he is confessing to something he can do. After the period, his word is not accepted, but he can still prove it by evidence (beyond reasonable doubt). Finally, the oath itself: if he swore for a specific period (e.g., four months), the oath drops after that period automatically. If he swore indefinitely (or absolutely), the oath remains.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation for breaking an oath by Allah; freeing a slave, feeding 10 poor, or clothing them.
بانت (bānat): She becomes separated by a bain (irrevocable) divorce.
الفقهاء (al-fuqahā’): Jurists; here includes Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the Ila' oath was for an unspecified duration (absolute) and the husband does not have intercourse for four months?
A) The oath remains after four months
B) Bain divorce occurs after four months
C) He must expiate without divorce
D) He can continue the oath indefinitely

Key Takeaway
In Ila', intercourse requires expiation; abstaining for four months results in an irrevocable bain divorce.

Effect of Ila' on Remarriage and Pregnancy
Explains effects of ila' on divorce and remarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the consequences of an oath of ila' when the husband remarries the same wife and when the wife is pregnant.

Core Idea
An oath of ila' applies only to the current marriage; a new marriage requires a new oath.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies how an oath of ila' (vow to abstain from intercourse) operates across multiple marriages and during pregnancy. It distinguishes between the original marriage and subsequent marriages, and explains that once a divorce occurs by ila', the same oath cannot cause another divorce during the waiting period. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly applying the rules of ila' in complex family situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key ruling about repeated marriages
Note that if a husband swears to abstain for four months, and later marries the same woman again, the old oath does not carry over. Each marriage has its own independent effect for ila'.
2
Analyze the scenario with a pregnant wife
Consider the case where a wife is pregnant and the husband takes an oath of ila'. The four-month period runs even during pregnancy; if she delivers after four months, divorce occurs by ila' and her iddah ends with delivery.
Delivery after four months triggers the divorce at the end of four months, not at delivery.
3
Understand the limitation during the iddah period
Once a divorce has occurred by ila', no further divorce occurs from the same oath during the iddah, even if another four months pass. The separation is complete for that marriage.
The oath is tied to the original marriage, not to the iddah period.
4
Note the linguistic clarification
The author explains that 'qurban' is a verbal noun meaning nearness, used here for intercourse. This clarifies the terminology used in the ruling.
Not essential for the ruling but aids accurate understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حلف على أربعة أشهر وبقيت لو على الأبد ولو نكحها ثانياً وثالثاً ومضت المدتان بلا الطلاق بأن يدعوها إلى الفراش فيحنث، ثم يقربها بعد ذلك من غير أن يحنث بالقربان. ولو قال لامرأته إن اغتسلت من جنابتي ما دمت امرأتي فأنت طالق ثلاثاً وأعاد هذا القول وكانت المرأة حاملاً ولم يقربها بعد المقالة حتى وضعت حملها بعد أربعة أشهر فصاعداً فإنها تبين بواحدة عند انقضاء أربعة أشهر لأنه كان مولياً وتنقضي عدتها بوضع الحمل، فإن تزوجها بعد ذلك لا يكون مولياً لو قربها لا يحنث لأن اليمين كانت موقتة إلى بقاء النكاح وبعدما وقعت تطليقة بالإيلاء لا يقع عليها طلاق آخر وإن مضت أربعة أشهر أخرى قبل وضع الحمل لأن المبانة بالإيلاء لا يقع عليها طلاق آخر بحكم ذلك الإيلاء وإن كانت في العدة ما لم تتزوج وتمامه في الخانية. وعلم أن القربان مصدر قرب يقرب من باب فعل بكسر العين في الماضي وفتحها في المضارع وله مصدران القربان والقرب بمعنى الدنو؛ كذا في ضياء الحلوم.
He swore for four months and it remains if for eternity, and if he marries her a second and third time and the two periods pass without intercourse, she becomes divorced by one divorce upon his calling her to bed and he breaks the oath, then he has intercourse with her after that without breaking the oath by the intercourse. And if he said to his wife, 'If I perform a major ablution from my sexual impurity as long as you are my wife, you are thrice divorced,' and he repeated this statement, and she was pregnant and he did not have intercourse with her after the statement until she delivered after four months or more, then she becomes irrevocably divorced by one divorce at the end of four months because he was a muli (one who takes an oath of abstention), and her waiting period ends with delivery. Then if he marries her after that, he does not become a muli; if he has intercourse with her, he does not break the oath because the oath was limited to the duration of the marriage. After one divorce occurred by ila', no further divorce occurs upon her even if another four months pass before delivery, because the woman separated by ila' does not have another divorce occur by virtue of that same ila' even if she is in the waiting period, unless she marries someone else. Its completion is in al-Khaniya. And know that 'qurban' is a verbal noun of 'qaruba yaqrubu' from the verb pattern 'fa'ala' with a kasra on the 'ayn in the past and fatha in the present, and it has two verbal nouns: 'qurban' and 'qurb' meaning nearness; as in Diya' al-Hulum.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq (Bahr al-Ra'iq) explaining the effects of an oath of ila' (vow to abstain from intercourse). The ruling: if a husband swears to abstain for exactly four months, and then remarries the same wife after divorce, the same rules apply for each new marriage. The oath is specific to that marriage. If the wife is pregnant and delivers after four months, she becomes divorced by the ila' and her waiting period ends with delivery. No further divorce occurs by the same ila' if another four months pass while she is in the waiting period, because the first divorce has already separated them for that marriage. The passage also includes a linguistic note that 'qurban' is a verbal noun meaning closeness.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A husband's oath to abstain from intercourse with his wife for four months or more.
القربان (al-qurbān): Verbal noun meaning intercourse or nearness, used here as a synonym for intercourse (jimā') in the context of ila'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a wife is pregnant and her husband takes an oath of ila', when does the divorce occur?
A) Immediately upon the oath
B) At the end of four months, regardless of delivery
C) At the time of delivery, if after four months
D) At the end of her pregnancy iddah

Key Takeaway
An oath of ila' is specific to the current marriage; it does not carry over to a subsequent marriage, and during the iddah, no further divorce from the same oath occurs.

Expiation and Irrevocable Divorce in Ila'
Expansion on ila' rulings with proof by consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of ila' regarding expiation and irrevocable divorce, and apply the rules of testimony to the husband's claim of intercourse.

Core Idea
In ila', intercourse within four months requires expiation; without it, the wife becomes irrevocably divorced by consensus.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding ila' (vow of abstinence). It clarifies two key outcomes: if the husband has intercourse during the designated period, expiation becomes wajib; if he does not, the marriage ends with a single irrevocable divorce. The discussion also addresses the husband's testimony about intercourse and its acceptance before or after the period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possible outcomes
Focus on the two branches: (1) husband has intercourse within the four months → expiation wajib; (2) no intercourse → wife becomes bain (irrevocably divorced). Note the legal effect of each.
The expiation is only for an oath by Allah; the divorce is by consensus (ijma).
2
Understand the expiation ruling
Examine when expiation becomes obligatory (lazima): only after actual intercourse, not before. The text clarifies that divine forgiveness for the sinful oath does not cancel the worldly legal obligation.
Expiation before intercourse is invalid, as mentioned by al-Asbijabi.
3
Analyze the irrevocable divorce
If no intercourse occurs, after four months the wife receives one irrevocable divorce. This is supported by consensus and narrations from several Companions.
The iddah (waiting period) begins from the time of irrevocability, not from the start of ila'.
4
Examine the rules of testimony
If the husband claims intercourse during the four months, his word is accepted. If he claims after the period, his word is not accepted, but he can prove it with evidence.
This is based on the principle that one's confession about an act they control is trustworthy, but after the deadline, it becomes suspect.
5
Apply the principles to new scenarios
Consider cases like the husband going mad then having intercourse, or the oath being eternal. Use the text's rulings to determine outcomes.
The text explicitly includes the madness scenario, showing the ruling is general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن وطئ في المدة كفّر بتشديد الفاء أي لزمته الكفارة إذا كانت يمينه بالله تعالى وبه قالت الأئمة الثلاثة ووعد المغفرة بسبب الفيء الذي هو مثل التوبة لا ينافي الزام الكفارة لأنه حكم دنيوي وذاك أخروي. قيد بالوطء لأنه لو كفر قبله لا يكون كفارة؛ كذا ذكر الأسبيجابي. وأطلق في الوطء فشمل ما إذا جن بعد الإيلاء ثم وطئها انحلت وسقط الإيلاء؛ كذا في فتح القدير قوله : وسقط الإيلاء بإجماع الفقهاء حتى لو مضت أربعة أشهر يقع طلاق لانحلال اليمين بالحنث وسواء حلف على أربعة أشهر أو أطلق أو على الأبد قوله : (وإلا بانت أي إن لم يطأ في المدة وهي أربعة أشهر وقعت عليه طلقة بائنة لأنه قد وقع التخلص من الظلم ولا يكون بالرجعي لأنه بسبيل من يردها إلى عصمته ويعبد الإيلاء فتعين البائن لتملك نفسها وتزول سلطنته عنها جزاء لظلمه وهو مروي عن عثمان بن عفان وزيد بن ثابت وعلي وابن مسعود وابن عباس وابن عمر رضي الله عنهم وتمامه في فتح القدير. وذكر الأسبيجابي أن العدة من وقت البينونة وبه فارق الطلاق الرجعي فإنه وإن أوجب بينونة في ثاني الحال كالإيلاء لكن العدة فيه من وقت الطلاق لا البينونة. وفي المبسوط : وإذا ادعى أنه قد جامعها فإن ادعى في الأربعة الأشهر فالقول قوله، وإن ادعى ذلك بعد مضي المدة لم يقبل قوله بناء على الأصل المعروف أنه متى أقر بما يملك انشاءه لا يكون متهماً، فلو أقام بينة على مقالته في الأربعة الأشهر أنه قد جامعها فهي امرأته لأن الثابت بإقراره كالثابت بالمعاينة وهي من أعجب المسائل أنه لا يقبل إقراره بعد مضي المدة ويتمكن من إثباته بالبينة ا هـ .
His statement: (If he has intercourse within the period, he must expiate, with the shadda on the fa') i.e., expiation becomes obligatory if his oath was by Allah Almighty, and the three Imams said this. And the promise of forgiveness due to the return (fay') which is like repentance does not negate the imposition of expiation because it is a worldly ruling while that is otherworldly. He restricted it to intercourse because if he expiates before it, it is not expiation; as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. And he left intercourse unrestricted, so it includes if he went mad after ila' then had intercourse, the ila' dissolves and falls; as in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (And the ila' falls by consensus of the jurists), so that if four months pass, divorce occurs due to the dissolution of the oath by breaking it, whether he swore for four months or absolutely or for eternity. His statement: (Otherwise she becomes irrevocably divorced) i.e., if he did not have intercourse within the period, which is four months, one irrevocable divorce occurs upon him because there has been deliverance from injustice, and it is not a revocable divorce because he is in a position to take her back into his protection and the object of ila' is absent, so the irrevocable divorce is determined so that she owns herself and his authority over her is removed as a penalty for his injustice, and this is narrated from Uthman ibn Affan, Zayd ibn Thabit, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, and Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them; its completion is in Fath al-Qadir. Al-Asbijabi mentioned that the waiting period is from the time of irrevocability, and this distinguishes it from revocable divorce, for although it causes irrevocability in the second instance like ila', the waiting period in it is from the time of divorce, not from irrevocability. In al-Mabsut: If he claims that he had intercourse with her, then if he claims during the four months, his word is accepted; if he claims after the period has passed, his word is not accepted based on the known principle that whenever one confesses to something he has the power to create, he is not accused. So if he brings evidence of his statement during the four months that he had intercourse with her, then she is his wife because what is established by his confession is like what is established by direct observation, and it is one of the most amazing issues that his confession is not accepted after the period has passed, but he can prove it by evidence. End.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ijma) and commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It covers two main points: (1) If the husband has intercourse within the four-month period of ila', he must expiate (kaffara) because his oath was by Allah. This expiation is a worldly legal consequence and does not conflict with divine forgiveness. The expiation becomes obligatory only after intercourse, not before. (2) If the husband does not have intercourse within the four months, the wife becomes irrevocably divorced (bain). This is by consensus of the jurists (ijma) as reported in the text, and it is based on the practice of several Companions. The waiting period (iddah) for such a divorce begins at the time of irrevocability, not at the time of divorce, unlike revocable divorce. The passage also discusses testimony: if the husband claims to have had intercourse during the four months, his word is accepted; if he claims after the period, his word is not accepted, but he can prove it with evidence.

Key Terms
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): Expiation for breaking an oath by Allah, which is either feeding ten poor people, clothing them, or freeing a slave, or fasting three days if unable.
البينونة (al-baynūnah): Irrevocability after divorce; the wife cannot be taken back without a new marriage contract.
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A vow of abstinence from marital intercourse for a period of at least four months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the husband has intercourse within the four-month ila' period?
A) Expiation is wajib
B) Divorce occurs
C) Both A and B
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In ila', intercourse within the period triggers expiation; without it, marriage ends in irrevocable divorce by consensus.

Perpetual Oath and Multiplicity in Ila'
Expansion of rulings on perpetual oath and multiplicity in ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between fixed-term and perpetual oaths in ila', apply the rule that a perpetual oath survives remarriage, and determine when divorce multiplies versus when expiation multiplies.

Core Idea
A perpetual oath in ila' remains effective after remarriage; divorce multiplies with separate periods, not with one fulfillment.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the rulings of oaths in ila'. It distinguishes between a time-bound oath that expires and a perpetual oath that continues, and it explores how multiple oaths and multiple marriages affect the occurrence of divorce and expiation. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi law in complex marital situations.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish fixed-term vs perpetual oath
Identify the key difference: a fixed-term oath (e.g., four months) expires and does not affect a new marriage; a perpetual oath (e.g., 'never') remains and applies to subsequent marriages to the same woman.
Based on the matn: 'وسقط اليمين لو حلف على أربعة أشهر' vs 'وبقيت لو على الأبد'.
2
Trace the effect of perpetual oath after remarriage
Follow the scenario: husband swears perpetual ila', divorces after 4 months, then remarries her after iddah. The oath remains, so after another 4 months without intercourse, she is divorced again. This can happen up to three times.
If she marries another husband and returns later, the original oath is invalidated.
3
Differentiate multiplicity of divorce vs expiation
Understand that when multiple oaths are pronounced, expiation multiplies with each distinct oath broken, but divorce multiplies only if separate periods pass. If a single period is fulfilled (birr), divorce does not multiply.
Example: 'كلما دخلت فوالله لا أقربك' leads to multiple divorces but one expiation if he breaks the oath once.
4
Note Zufar's disagreement and the tarjih
Zufar holds that divorce multiplies with multiplicity of periods even if one fulfillment, but the mufta bihi view is that it does not. Al-Ramli indicates the matn's view is chosen.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

قوله : (وسقط اليمين لو حلف على أربعة أشهر) لأنها موقتة بوقت فلا تبقى بعد مضيه قوله : ( وبقيت لو على الأبد أي بقيت اليمين لو كان حلف على الأبد سواء صرح به أو أطلق فيء بانت بأخريين فإن نكحها بعد زوج آخر لم تطلق فلو وطئها كفر لبقاء اليمين ولا لعدم ما يبطلها من حنث أو مضى وقت قوله : (فلو نكحها ثانياً وثالثاً ومضت المدتان بلا فيء بانت بأخريين) يعني لو تزوجها بعدما بانت بالإيلاء ثم مضت المدة بعد التزوج الثاني بانت بتطليقة أخرى. وكذا لو تزوجها بعد ذلك ثالثاً ومضت المدة بانت بثالثة. وتعتبر المدة من وقت التزوج لأن به يثبت حقها في الجماع وبامتناعه صار ظالماً فيجازي بإزالة نعمة النكاح. وأشار إلى أنه لا يتكرر الطلاق قبل التزوج لأنه لا حق لها في الجماع قبله وهو الأصح بخلاف ما لو أبانها بتنجيز الطلاق ثم مضت مدة الإيلاء وهي في العدة حيث تقع أخرى بالإيلاء لأنه بمنزلة التعليق بمضي الزمان والمعلق لا يبطل بتنجيز ما دون الثلاث. وفي الظهيرية : لو قال والله لا أقربك أبداً فمضت أربعة أشهر ووقع الطلاق ثم مضت أربعة أشهر أخرى وهي في العدة تقع أخرى، وكذلك هذا في الكرة الثالثة. ولو تزوجها بعد انقضاء العدة تعتبر مدة الإيلاء الثاني من وقت التزوج، ولو تزوجها في من وقت العدة تعتبر وقوع الطلاق الأول ا قوله : (فإن نكحها بعد زواج آخر لم تطلق) لتقييده بطلاق هذا الملك وقد انتهى بالثلاث سواء وقعت متفرقة بسبب الإيلاء المؤبد أو نجزها بعد الإيلاء قبل مضي مدته ثم عادت إليه بعد زوج آخر لبطلان الإيلاء فلا يعود بالتزوج قوله : (فلو وطئها كفر لبقاء اليمين) أي لو وطئها بعد ما عادت إليه بعد زوج آخر لزمه التكفير عن يمينه لبقائها في حقه وإن لم يبق في حق الطلاق وفي الجامع الكبير للصدر الشهيد: الإيلاء يصح في المنكرة حلف لا يقرب إحداهما ومضت المدة بانت واحدة ،ويخير فإن مضت مدة أخرى قبله بانت الأخرى للتعيين ودلت أن الإيلاء يبطل بالبينونة وأنه لا ينعقد على المبانة في العدة وهو الأصح بخلاف الإبانة بغيره، وعلى هذا تكرار مدة الواحدة بخلاف كلما مضت أربعة أشهر فأنت بائن ينوي الطلاق اهـ. ومن باب اليمين في الأيلاء طلاقاً . ويتعدد بتعدد المدة وكفارة في الحنث وتتعدد بتعدد الاسم. قال كلما دخلت واحدة من هاتين الدارين فوالله لا أقربك ودخلها، أو قال كلما دخلت هذه ودخلها مرتين يتعدد في حق الطلاق دون الكفارة، ولو قال فعلي يمين إن قربتك تعددا قال في مجلس مرتين إذا جاء غد فوالله لا أقربك تعدد الكفارة بالوطء لتعدد الاسم والطلاق بالبر لا لاتحاد المدة، وعند زفر تتعدد، ولو علقه بوقتين تعدداً لتعددهما . قال كلما دخلت فأنت طالق ثلاثاً إن قربتك أو فعبدي هذا . حر يتعدد الإيلاء والجزاء متحد لتعذره. قال كلما دخلت فإن قربتك فعلي يمين أو نذر أو حجة يتعدد ويشترط مع كل دخلة قربان للعطف . قال كلما دخلت فوالله لا أقربك أو قدم القسم يتعدد الطلاق يوجب قوله : (وفي الظهيرية لو قال والله لا أقربك أبداً الخ قال الرملي : أشار رحمه الله تعالى بنقله عنها إلى أن في المسألة قولين وما فيها ضعيف والمختار ما في المتن قوله: (والطلاق بالبر لا) أي لا يتعدد وقوله لاتحاد البر علة له.
His statement: (And the oath expires if he swore for four months) because it is tied to a time, so it does not remain after it passes. His statement: (And it remains if for eternity) i.e., the oath remains if he swore for eternity, whether he explicitly said so or was absolute. So she becomes divorced by another divorce; if he marries her after another husband, she is not divorced; so if he has intercourse with her, he must expiate because the oath remains, and there is nothing to invalidate it, whether breaking the oath or passage of time. His statement: (So if he marries her a second and third time and the two periods pass without intercourse, she becomes divorced by another two divorces) means if he marries her after she became irrevocably divorced by ila', then the period passes after the second marriage, she becomes divorced by another divorce. Likewise, if he marries her a third time and the period passes, she becomes divorced by a third. And the period is counted from the time of marriage because by it her right to intercourse is established, and by his abstention he becomes oppressive, so he is penalized by removal of the blessing of marriage. And he indicated that the divorce does not recur before marriage because she has no right to intercourse before it, and this is the correct view, contrary to the case where he divorces her irrevocably by an immediate divorce, then the ila' period passes while she is in the waiting period, because another divorce occurs by ila' because it is like a conditional suspended on the passage of time, and what is suspended is not invalidated by an immediate divorce less than three. And in al-Dhahiriyya: If he said, 'By Allah, I will never have intercourse with you,' then four months pass and divorce occurs, then another four months pass while she is in the waiting period, another divorce occurs, and likewise for the third time. If he marries her after the waiting period ends, the second ila' period is counted from the time of marriage; if he marries her during the waiting period, it is counted from the first divorce. His statement: (If he marries her after another husband, she is not divorced) because it is restricted to the divorce of this ownership and it has ended with three, whether they occurred separately due to perpetual ila' or he effected them after ila' before its period passed, then she returned to him after another husband because the ila' is invalid, so it does not return with marriage. His statement: (So if he has intercourse with her, he must expiate because the oath remains) i.e., if he has intercourse with her after she returned to him after another husband, expiation for his oath becomes obligatory because it remains in his regard, even if it does not remain regarding divorce. And in al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sadr al-Shahid: Ila' is valid concerning a woman whose marriage is invalid; if he swears not to have intercourse with one of them and the period passes, one becomes irrevocably divorced, and he is given a choice; if another period passes before him, the other becomes irrevocably divorced for determination; and it indicates that ila' is invalidated by irrevocability and that it is not contracted on a woman who is irrevocably divorced in the waiting period, and this is the correct view, contrary to separation by other means. On this basis, the period is repeated for one woman, contrary to the case where he says, 'Whenever four months pass, you are irrevocable,' intending divorce. And from the chapter of oaths in ila': Divorce multiplies with multiplicity of periods, and expiation in breaking the oath multiplies with multiplicity of names. He said: 'Whenever you enter one of these two houses, by Allah I will not have intercourse with you,' and she enters them, or he said, 'Whenever you enter this,' and she enters it twice, it multiplies in regard to divorce but not expiation. If he said, 'I have an oath if I have intercourse with you,' it multiplies. He said in one session twice: 'When tomorrow comes, by Allah I will not have intercourse with you,' the expiation multiplies by intercourse due to multiplicity of the name, but divorce does not multiply due to unity of the period. According to Zufar, it multiplies. If he suspends it on two times, it multiplies due to their multiplicity. He said: 'Whenever you enter, you are thrice divorced if I have intercourse with you' or 'this my slave is free,' the ila' multiplies but the consequence is one because it is impossible. He said: 'Whenever you enter, if I have intercourse with you, I have an oath or a vow or a pilgrimage,' it multiplies, and each entry requires a new act of intercourse due to conjunction. He said: 'Whenever you enter, by Allah I will not have intercourse with you' or he placed the oath first, the divorce multiplies. His statement: (In al-Dhahiriyya: If he said, 'By Allah, I will never have intercourse with you'...) al-Ramli said: By his transmission from it, may Allah have mercy on him, he indicated that there are two opinions on the issue, and what is in it is weak, and the chosen is what is in the text. His statement: (And divorce by the fulfillment does not multiply) i.e., it does not multiply, and his statement: 'due to unity of fulfillment' is the reason for it.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with some proof by analogy and istihsan. It is part of the commentary on the matn, explaining the effects of a perpetual oath (ila' for eternity) versus a time-bound oath. The key ruling: if the oath is for eternity, it remains after the first divorce; if the husband remarries the same woman after the waiting period, the same ila' applies again, causing another divorce after four months, and then a third. However, if she married another man in between and then returns to him, the original ila' is invalidated and does not revive. Regarding multiplicity, the passage discusses how divorce and expiation multiply based on the wording of the oath. For example, if he says 'By Allah, I will not have intercourse with you,' and repeats that oath, the expiation multiplies if he breaks it, but the divorce may not multiply if the period is the same. The text also notes a difference with Zufar and mentions a weak opinion from al-Dhahiriyya, but the preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that stated in the matn. The commentary by al-Ramli clarifies that the multiplication of divorce depends on the fulfillment (birr) being one act, so if he breaks the oath multiple times, divorce does not multiply if the oath was one.

Key Terms
اليمين المؤبد (al-yamīn al-mu'abbad): An oath that is not limited to a specific time, such as swearing 'by Allah I will never have intercourse with you'.
البر (al-birr): Fulfillment of the oath by not breaking it (i.e., abstaining from intercourse) as opposed to breaking it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a man swears 'By Allah, I will never have intercourse with you' (perpetual oath) and divorces by ila' after four months, then remarries her after her iddah, what happens after another four months without intercourse?
A) She is not divorced because the oath already caused divorce
B) She is divorced by one more divorce
C) She is divorced by three divorces all at once
D) The husband must expiate but she is not divorced

Key Takeaway
A perpetual oath in ila' continues beyond the first divorce and applies to subsequent marriages to the same woman, but is invalidated if she marries another man; multiplicity of divorce depends on separate periods, not on one fulfillment.

Remarriage After Ila: The Beginning of a New Period
Ruling on remarriage after ila and start of new period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on when a new ila period begins upon remarriage and identify whether talaq occurs before remarriage.

Core Idea
Remarrying an ex-wife after ila starts a new period; talaq does not occur before remarriage.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a man divorces his wife by ila, then later remarries her. Does the original ila continue? The Hanafi school teaches that a new, independent ila period begins only upon remarriage. Understanding this is crucial for determining when divorce actually occurs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial divorce and remarriage
The man divorces by ila (period passes). He then marries her again. Note that the original ila has already resulted in a talaq.
2
Determine when the new period starts
The text states: 'وتعتبر المدة من وقت التزوج' — the period is considered from the time of the new marriage, not from the original oath.
This is because her right to intercourse revives only upon remarriage.
3
Apply the ruling to multiple marriages
If he marries her a second and third time, each new marriage starts a new period; after each period passes without intercourse, a talaq occurs.
Thus, three rounds of remarriage and abstention can produce three total divorces.
4
Distinguish from immediate talaq
If the original divorce was by immediate talaq (talaq mubanah), the ila period during idda can still cause another talaq because it is a conditional suspended on time.
The text says: 'لأنه بمنزلة التعليق بمضي الزمان والمعلق لا يبطل بتنجيز ما دون الثلاث.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لبطلان الإيلاء فلا يعود بالتزوج قوله : (فلو وطئها كفر لبقاء اليمين) أي لو وطئها بعد ما عادت إليه بعد زوج آخر لزمه التكفير عن يمينه لبقائها في حقه وإن لم يبق في حق الطلاق وفي الجامع الكبير للصدر الشهيد: الإيلاء يصح في المنكرة حلف لا يقرب إحداهما ومضت المدة بانت واحدة ،ويخير فإن مضت مدة أخرى قبله بانت الأخرى للتعيين ودلت أن الإيلاء يبطل بالبينونة وأنه لا ينعقد على المبانة في العدة وهو الأصح بخلاف الإبانة بغيره، وعلى هذا تكرار مدة الواحدة بخلاف كلما مضت أربعة أشهر فأنت بائن ينوي الطلاق اهـ. ومن باب اليمين في الأيلاء طلاقاً . ويتعدد بتعدد المدة وكفارة في الحنث وتتعدد بتعدد الاسم. قال كلما دخلت واحدة من هاتين الدارين فوالله لا أقربك ودخلها، أو قال كلما دخلت هذه ودخلها مرتين يتعدد في حق الطلاق دون الكفارة، ولو قال فعلي يمين إن قربتك تعددا قال في مجلس مرتين إذا جاء غد فوالله لا أقربك تعدد الكفارة بالوطء لتعدد الاسم والطلاق بالبر لا لاتحاد المدة، وعند زفر تتعدد، ولو علقه بوقتين تعدداً لتعددهما . قال كلما دخلت فأنت طالق ثلاثاً إن قربتك أو فعبدي هذا . حر يتعدد الإيلاء والجزاء متحد لتعذره. قال كلما دخلت فإن قربتك فعلي يمين أو نذر أو حجة يتعدد ويشترط مع كل دخلة قربان للعطف . قال كلما دخلت فوالله لا أقربك أو قدم القسم يتعدد الطلاق يوجب قوله : (وفي الظهيرية لو قال والله لا أقربك أبداً الخ قال الرملي : أشار رحمه الله تعالى بنقله عنها إلى أن في المسألة قولين وما فيها ضعيف والمختار ما في المتن قوله: (والطلاق بالبر لا) أي لا يتعدد وقوله لاتحاد البر علة له .
He said: (If he marries her a second and third time and the two periods pass without intercourse, she becomes irrevocably divorced by the last two). Meaning if he marries her after she became divorced by ila, then the period passes after the second marriage, she becomes divorced by another talaq. Similarly if he marries her a third time and the period passes, she becomes divorced by a third. The period is considered from the time of marriage because by it her right to intercourse is established, and by his abstention he becomes oppressive, so he is punished by removing the blessing of marriage. He indicated that talaq does not repeat before marriage because she has no right to intercourse before it, and this is the most correct view, contrary to the case where he divorces her by immediate talaq then the period of ila passes while she is in idda, where another talaq occurs by ila because it is like a conditional suspended on the passing of time, and what is conditional is not invalidated by executing less than three. In al-Zahiriyya: If he said, 'By Allah I will not approach you forever,' then four months passed and talaq occurred, then another four months passed while she is in idda, another talaq occurs, and similarly in the third round. If he marries her after the idda expires, the second ila period is considered from the time of marriage. If he marries her during the idda, the occurrence of the first talaq is considered... He said: (If he marries her after another husband, she is not divorced) because it is restricted to the talaq of this marriage, and it has ended with three, whether they occurred separately due to perpetual ila or he executed them after ila before its period passed, then she returns to him after another husband, because ila is invalidated, so it does not return by marriage. He said: (If he has intercourse with her, he must expiate due to the remaining oath) meaning if he has intercourse with her after she returned to him after another husband, he must expiate for his oath because it remains in his effect, even though it does not remain regarding talaq. In al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sadr al-Shahid: Ila is valid regarding a woman who is not known; he swore not to approach one of them, then the period passed, she becomes divorced by one, and he is given choice; if another period passes before him, the other becomes divorced by specification. And it indicates that ila is invalidated by separation and that it is not contracted on a woman in idda who is divorced, and this is the most correct view, contrary to separation by other means. Upon this, repeating the period of one is like every time four months pass, you are divorced, intending talaq. From the chapter of oaths in ila: talaq. And it multiplies with the multiplicity of the period, and expiation in breaking the oath multiplies with the multiplicity of the name. He said: 'Every time you enter one of these two houses, by Allah I will not approach you' and she entered, or he said 'Every time you enter this' and she entered twice, it multiplies regarding talaq but not expiation. If he said 'Upon me is an oath if I approach you' and he said it twice in one sitting, 'When tomorrow comes, by Allah I will not approach you,' expiation multiplies due to intercourse due to the multiplicity of the name, and talaq occurs by the oath [that is kept] because of the unity of the period, and according to Zufar it multiplies. If he suspended it on two times, it multiplies due to their multiplicity. He said: 'Every time you enter, you are divorced three if I approach you' or 'my slave is free,' the ila multiplies but the penalty is one because it is impossible [to multiply]. He said: 'Every time you enter, if I approach you, upon me is an oath or a vow or a pilgrimage,' it multiplies and intercourse is required with each entry due to the conjunction. He said: 'Every time you enter, by Allah I will not approach you' or he presented the oath, talaq multiplies and necessitates... He said: (In al-Zahiriyya: If he said 'By Allah I will not approach you forever' ... al-Ramli said: The author indicated by quoting it that there are two opinions in the issue, and what is in it is weak, and the chosen view is what is in the text. He said: (And talaq by keeping the oath does not multiply) i.e., it does not multiply, and his statement 'because of the unity of the oath' is the reason.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the rulings of ila when a man marries his ex-wife after separation. The author explains that if a man divorces his wife by ila (oath of abstention), then marries her again, a new ila period begins from the time of remarriage. If he marries her a second and third time and the periods pass without intercourse, she becomes divorced by two additional talaqs, totaling three. The period is counted from the new marriage because only then does the wife's right to intercourse revive. The author notes that talaq does not occur before the remarriage because she had no right to intercourse during the separation. However, if the man had divorced her by an immediate talaq and then the ila period passed during her idda, another talaq would occur because the conditional talaq is not invalidated by a prior lesser talaq. The text then quotes from al-Zahiriyya regarding an eternal oath: if a man swears never to approach his wife and four months pass resulting in talaq, then another four months pass while she is in idda, another talaq occurs, and similarly a third time. If he marries her after idda, a new ila period starts from the marriage. The author then discusses the case where a man marries his ex-wife after she has been married to another husband; in that case, she is not divorced by the old ila because the marriage has ended with three talaqs, and ila is invalidated. However, if he has intercourse with her, he must expiate for his oath because the oath remains in effect for kaffarah even if not for talaq. The passage then shifts to general principles of multiplicity in ila oaths, quoting from al-Jami' al-Kabir that ila can be valid for multiple wives, and explaining how talaq and kaffarah multiply based on the number of periods and names of Allah. Various examples are given, such as conditional oaths with multiple entries, and the view of Zufar who differs on some points. Finally, the author cites al-Ramli's comment that the relied-upon view is that talaq by keeping the oath does not multiply because the period is single.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A husband's oath to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more.
المدة (al-mudda): The period of four months that the husband must wait without intercourse, after which divorce occurs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man divorces his wife by ila, then marries her again, when does the new ila period begin?
A) From the time of the original oath
B) From the time of remarriage
C) From the time of the first missed intercourse
D) From the time of the original divorce

Key Takeaway
A new ila period begins upon remarriage; talaq does not occur before remarriage.

Multiplicity of Talaq by Keeping the Oath: The Principle of Unity of Period
Ruling on non-multiplication of talaq by keeping the oath and the dispute with Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that talaq by keeping the oath (al-talaq bi al-barr) does not multiply and evaluate the opposing view of Zufar.

Core Idea
Talaq achieved by keeping the oath does not multiply because the period is single.

This lesson delves into the debate over whether talaq multiplies when a man keeps his oath of abstention over multiple periods. The Hanafi school, relying on the unity of the period, holds that only one talaq occurs. Imam Zufar differs, and understanding his reasoning sharpens our grasp of the school's principles.

Guided Path
1
Define al-talaq bi al-barr
It is the divorce that results from the husband keeping his oath (i.e., not approaching his wife during the period). This is different from talaq that occurs when the husband breaks his oath by having intercourse.
2
State the Hanafi rule
This talaq does not multiply even if multiple periods pass. The text says: 'والطلاق بالبر لا يتعدد' (talaq by keeping the oath does not multiply).
3
Identify the basis (illa)
The reason given is 'لاتحاد المدة' (because of the unity of the period). The period is one continuous time frame stemming from one oath.
4
Contrast with Zufar's view
Zufar holds that it multiplies with each period. The text says: 'وعند زفر تتعدد' (and according to Zufar it multiplies). His reasoning is that each passing period is a separate event.
5
Apply to examples from the text
The text gives various examples: conditional oaths with multiple entries, where talaq multiplies but expiation may or may not. However, for talaq bi al-barr, multiplication is denied.
The later examples illustrate that talaq can multiply in other contexts (e.g., multiple entries) but not for simply keeping an oath.

He said: (If he marries her a second and third time and the two periods pass without intercourse, she becomes irrevocably divorced by the last two). Meaning if he marries her after she became divorced by ila, then the period passes after the second marriage, she becomes divorced by another talaq. Similarly if he marries her a third time and the period passes, she becomes divorced by a third. The period is considered from the time of marriage because by it her right to intercourse is established, and by his abstention he becomes oppressive, so he is punished by removing the blessing of marriage. He indicated that talaq does not repeat before marriage because she has no right to intercourse before it, and this is the most correct view, contrary to the case where he divorces her by immediate talaq then the period of ila passes while she is in idda, where another talaq occurs by ila because it is like a conditional suspended on the passing of time, and what is conditional is not invalidated by executing less than three. In al-Zahiriyya: If he said, 'By Allah I will not approach you forever,' then four months passed and talaq occurred, then another four months passed while she is in idda, another talaq occurs, and similarly in the third round. If he marries her after the idda expires, the second ila period is considered from the time of marriage. If he marries her during the idda, the occurrence of the first talaq is considered... He said: (If he marries her after another husband, she is not divorced) because it is restricted to the talaq of this marriage, and it has ended with three, whether they occurred separately due to perpetual ila or he executed them after ila before its period passed, then she returns to him after another husband, because ila is invalidated, so it does not return by marriage. He said: (If he has intercourse with her, he must expiate due to the remaining oath) meaning if he has intercourse with her after she returned to him after another husband, he must expiate for his oath because it remains in his effect, even though it does not remain regarding talaq. In al-Jami' al-Kabir by al-Sadr al-Shahid: Ila is valid regarding a woman who is not known; he swore not to approach one of them, then the period passed, she becomes divorced by one, and he is given choice; if another period passes before him, the other becomes divorced by specification. And it indicates that ila is invalidated by separation and that it is not contracted on a woman in idda who is divorced, and this is the most correct view, contrary to separation by other means. Upon this, repeating the period of one is like every time four months pass, you are divorced, intending talaq. From the chapter of oaths in ila: talaq. And it multiplies with the multiplicity of the period, and expiation in breaking the oath multiplies with the multiplicity of the name. He said: 'Every time you enter one of these two houses, by Allah I will not approach you' and she entered, or he said 'Every time you enter this' and she entered twice, it multiplies regarding talaq but not expiation. If he said 'Upon me is an oath if I approach you' and he said it twice in one sitting, 'When tomorrow comes, by Allah I will not approach you,' expiation multiplies due to intercourse due to the multiplicity of the name, and talaq occurs by the oath [that is kept] because of the unity of the period, and according to Zufar it multiplies. If he suspended it on two times, it multiplies due to their multiplicity. He said: 'Every time you enter, you are divorced three if I approach you' or 'my slave is free,' the ila multiplies but the penalty is one because it is impossible [to multiply]. He said: 'Every time you enter, if I approach you, upon me is an oath or a vow or a pilgrimage,' it multiplies and intercourse is required with each entry due to the conjunction. He said: 'Every time you enter, by Allah I will not approach you' or he presented the oath, talaq multiplies and necessitates... He said: (In al-Zahiriyya: If he said 'By Allah I will not approach you forever' ... al-Ramli said: The author indicated by quoting it that there are two opinions in the issue, and what is in it is weak, and the chosen view is what is in the text. He said: (And talaq by keeping the oath does not multiply) i.e., it does not multiply, and his statement 'because of the unity of the oath' is the reason.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the rulings of ila when a man marries his ex-wife after separation. The author explains that if a man divorces his wife by ila (oath of abstention), then marries her again, a new ila period begins from the time of remarriage. If he marries her a second and third time and the periods pass without intercourse, she becomes divorced by two additional talaqs, totaling three. The period is counted from the new marriage because only then does the wife's right to intercourse revive. The author notes that talaq does not occur before the remarriage because she had no right to intercourse during the separation. However, if the man had divorced her by an immediate talaq and then the ila period passed during her idda, another talaq would occur because the conditional talaq is not invalidated by a prior lesser talaq. The text then quotes from al-Zahiriyya regarding an eternal oath: if a man swears never to approach his wife and four months pass resulting in talaq, then another four months pass while she is in idda, another talaq occurs, and similarly a third time. If he marries her after idda, a new ila period starts from the marriage. The author then discusses the case where a man marries his ex-wife after she has been married to another husband; in that case, she is not divorced by the old ila because the marriage has ended with three talaqs, and ila is invalidated. However, if he has intercourse with her, he must expiate for his oath because the oath remains in effect for kaffarah even if not for talaq. The passage then shifts to general principles of multiplicity in ila oaths, quoting from al-Jami' al-Kabir that ila can be valid for multiple wives, and explaining how talaq and kaffarah multiply based on the number of periods and names of Allah. Various examples are given, such as conditional oaths with multiple entries, and the view of Zufar who differs on some points. Finally, the author cites al-Ramli's comment that the relied-upon view is that talaq by keeping the oath does not multiply because the period is single.

Key Terms
الطلاق بالبر (al-ṭalāq bi al-barr): Divorce that occurs because the husband kept his oath by not approaching his wife during the period.
اتحاد المدة (ittiḥād al-mudda): Unity of the period; the period from the oath is considered one continuous time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the effect of multiple periods passing without intercourse in a single oath of ila?
A) Multiple talaqs (one per period)
B) Only one talaq
C) Talaq occurs only after the first period
D) No talaq occurs

Key Takeaway
Talaq by keeping the oath does not multiply; the unity of the period is the governing principle.

The Minimum Period for Ila: Four Months or More
Establishes the minimum period for ila and analyzes an example oath with multiple periods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that ila requires a minimum of four months and explain the proof from the fatwa of Ibn Abbas, distinguishing between the apparent meaning of the verse and the relied-upon interpretation.

Core Idea
Ila is only valid for four months or more; less than four months is not ila.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a key condition for the validity of ila (an oath of abstinence). The matn states: 'No ila for less than four months.' While the Quranic verse (2:226) mentions a waiting period of four months, the Hanafi school relies on the interpretation of Ibn Abbas to conclude that the oath itself must be for at least four months. This lesson unpacks the proof, addresses a logical objection, and illustrates the ruling with an example oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage begins by stating the ruling: 'No ila for less than four months.' Note that this applies to a free woman; the ruling for a slave woman is given separately.
The ruling is a condition of validity, not just a recommendation.
2
Locate the Primary Proof
The primary proof is the Quranic verse (2:226) which mentions a waiting period of four months for those who swear ila. However, the verse does not explicitly state that the oath itself must be for four months.
The verse is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah regarding the minimum duration.
3
Understand the Hanafi Interpretation
The Hanafi school follows the fatwa of Ibn Abbas, who interpreted the verse to mean that ila is only valid when the husband swears to abstain for four months or more. This interpretation restricts the apparent generality of the verse.
Ibn Abbas's fatwa is considered an authoritative interpretation (tafsir) of the verse.
4
Analyze the Objection from Fath al-Qadir
The commentator notes that some scholars object that using the meaning (that the husband cannot approach without penalty) to prove the four-month minimum is a petition of principle (musadara). The response in al-Inaya clarifies that the basis is the fatwa of Ibn Abbas, not rational inference.
This shows the importance of relying on transmitted interpretation (tafsir) over pure reasoning.
5
Apply to an Example: Multiple Periods
The passage analyzes an oath: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months.' This is considered ila because the conjunction 'wa' combines the two periods into one continuous four-month period. If the negation or oath is repeated, it becomes two separate oaths.
This illustrates how the structure of the oath determines whether it qualifies as ila.

قوله : (ولا إيلاء فيما دون أربعة أشهر) يعني في الحرة بدليل أنه سيذكر حكم الأمة وبه قال الأئمة الأربعة وظاهر الآية صحة الإيلاء فيما دونها لأنه إنما خص بالأربعة مدة التربص وأما الحلف فمطلق، وما ذكره إيلاء) لأن الجمع بحرف الجمع كالجمع بلفظه وقوله بعد هذين الشهرين قيد اتفاقي لأنه لو لم يذكره كان الحكم كذلك. قيد بالواو بدون تكرار النفي والقسم لأنه لو كرر النفي بأن قال والله لا أقربك شهرين ولا شهرين وحكم اليمين كحكم الإيلاء في عدم التعدد إذا كانت بالواو فقط والتعدد إذا تكرر حرف النفي أو القسم، ولا فرق في تكرار القسم بين تكرار المقسم عليه أو لا حتى لو قال والله والله لا أفعل كذا فهو يمينان في ظاهر الرواية كقوله والله لا أفعل كذا والله لا أفعل كذا واعلم أنه لا تلازم بين كونه إيلاء ويميناً فلذلك قد يتعدد البر والحنث وقد يتحدان وقد يتعدد البر ويتحد الحنث وقلبه مثال الأول : إذا جاء غد فوالله لا بعد الغد تجب كفارتان وإن قربها في الغد تجب كفارة واحدة ومثال الثاني : والله لا أقربك أربعة أشهر وكذا مسألة الكتاب. قوله : (فمصادرة كما في فتح القدير ونصه والمعنى الذي ذكره هو أن المولى من لا يقدر على القربان في المدة إلا بشيء لزمه وهذا ليس كذلك فرع كون أقل المدة أربعة أشهر وإلا فنحن لا نقول به إذ قلنا بعدم تقييد المدة المحلوف عليها بها، فإثبات كون الأقل أربعة أشهر به مصادرة قوله : وتمامه في (العناية قال فيها : فإن قيل فتوى ابن عباس رضي الله تعالى عنهما مخالف لظاهر النص لأن الله تعالى قال للذين يؤلون من نسائهم تربص أربعة أشهر ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٢٦] أطلق الإيلاء وقيد التربص بمدة وذلك يقتضي أن من He said: (And there is no ila for less than four months) meaning for a free woman, as evidence that he will mention the ruling for a slave woman. And this is the view of the four imams. The apparent meaning of the verse supports the validity of ila for less than four months because the verse only specifies four months as the period of waiting, while the oath is absolute. And the meaning mentioned by the commentator and others is a petition of principle, as in Fath al-Qadir. However, our shaykhs adhere to the fatwa of Ibn Abbas as an interpretation of the verse. The remainder is in al-Inaya. And Allah knows best. He said: (By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months - this is ila) because joining with a conjunction is like joining with the word itself. His statement 'after these two months' is an incidental qualification because even if he did not mention it, the ruling would be the same. He restricted it with 'wa' without repeating the negation and oath because if he repeated the negation by saying 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months nor two months' or repeated the oath by saying 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months, by Allah, I will not approach you for two months,' it would not be ila because they are two oaths whose periods overlap. So if he approaches her before two months pass, two expiations are obligatory; if he approaches after they pass, no expiation is obligatory because the periods have ended. The ruling of an oath is like the ruling of ila in that there is no multiplicity if it is only with 'wa', and multiplicity if the negation or oath is repeated. There is no difference in repeating the oath between repeating the sworn matter or not; even if he says 'By Allah, by Allah, I will not do such-and-such,' it is two oaths in the apparent narration, like his saying 'By Allah, I will not do such-and-such, by Allah, I will not do such-and-such.' Know that there is no necessary connection between being ila and being an oath; therefore, sometimes the bar and the hanth (fulfillment and violation) multiply, and sometimes they are single, and sometimes the bar multiplies and the hanth is single, and vice versa. Example of the first: 'When tomorrow comes, by Allah I will not approach you; when the day after tomorrow comes, by Allah I will not approach you.' Then ila multiplies due to the multiplicity of the period, and the oath multiplies due to the multiplicity of the mention. If he leaves her for four months from the first day, he fulfills the first and she becomes divorced. Then when another day passes, he fulfills the second and she is also divorced. If he approaches her after the day after tomorrow, two expiations are obligatory; if he approaches her on the morrow, only one expiation is obligatory. Example of the second: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months,' and likewise the issue in the book. He said: (It is a petition of principle, as in Fath al-Qadir, and its text: The meaning that he mentioned is that the one who does ila is one who cannot approach his wife during the period except with something that becomes obligatory for him, and this is not the case. This is a branch of the condition that the minimum period is four months; otherwise, we do not say it, since we say that the period sworn is not restricted to it. So proving that the minimum is four months by this is a petition of principle. He said: And its completion is in al-Inaya, where it says: If it is said that the fatwa of Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, contradicts the apparent meaning of the text because Allah said: 'For those who swear to abstain from their wives, a waiting period of four months' (2:226). He mentioned ila absolutely and restricted the waiting period to a time, which implies that whoever swears to abstain from his wife, even for a short period like a day or an hour, must wait four months. So restricting the period is an addition to the text, and it is not permissible by the fatwa of Ibn Abbas. The answer is that the fatwa of Ibn...

Commentary
This passage addresses the fundamental condition that ila is only valid when the husband swears to abstain for four months or more. The matn states 'No ila for less than four months,' meaning for a free woman; the ruling for a slave woman will follow. The commentator notes that the four imams agree on this, although the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse (2:226) might suggest that ila is valid for any period, with the four months being the waiting period. However, the Hanafi school follows the interpretation of Ibn Abbas (RA), who restricted ila to four months or more. The text then analyzes an example oath: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months.' This is considered ila because the conjunction 'wa' combines the two periods into one continuous period of four months. If the husband repeated the negation or the oath, it would be two separate oaths, and the ruling would differ. The passage also discusses the relationship between ila and oaths, explaining that they are not coextensive; sometimes one multiplies while the other does not. Examples are given to illustrate when multiple expiations are required versus multiple divorces. Finally, the commentator addresses a potential objection from Fath al-Qadir about the reasoning being a petition of principle, and refers to al-Inaya for the complete answer involving Ibn Abbas's fatwa.

Key Terms
التربص (al-tarabbus): The waiting period of four months that the husband must observe after swearing ila.
المصادرة (al-muṣādara): Petition of principle; arguing in a circle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum duration for an ila oath to be valid?
A) One month
B) Two months
C) Three months
D) Four months

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a minimum of four months for ila, based on the fatwa of Ibn Abbas, ensuring that only oaths with harmful intent of prolonged abstinence trigger the waiting period and potential divorce.

The Condition of Four Months for Ila'
Commentary on the matn ruling that there is no ila' for less than four months for a free woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for a valid ila' and explain the proof from the fatwa of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
An oath of abstinence only becomes ila' if it is for four months or more.

The matn states that there is no ila' for less than four months. The commentator explains this applies to free women and notes agreement among the four imams. He then addresses a potential objection from the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse and clarifies the Hanafi reliance on the interpretation of Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State that the matn rules: 'There is no ila' for less than four months' – meaning an oath of abstinence for a shorter duration does not constitute ila'.
This applies to free women; a slave woman's ruling will be given separately.
2
Locate the Proof
The commentator cites the Quran verse (2:226) and the fatwa of Ibn Abbas. The verse prescribes a four-month waiting period for those who take an oath, but the Hanafi school uses Ibn Abbas's interpretation to set the minimum oath duration.
The proof is a combination of a Quranic text and a companion's interpretation.
3
Analyze the Apparent Objection
The verse seems to allow any oath duration because it mentions a waiting period after the oath, not a minimum for the oath itself. The commentator notes this apparent meaning.
This objection is why some might think a shorter oath could be ila'.
4
Understand the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi school does not rely on the apparent meaning alone. Instead, it follows the fatwa of Ibn Abbas, which is considered a binding interpretation (tafsir) of the verse.
The commentator rejects alternative reasoning as circular (مصادرة) and directs to al-Inaya for details.
5
Conclude the Legal Effect
An oath for less than four months does not trigger the four-month waiting period. The wife cannot claim ila' or seek judicial separation based on such an oath.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

قوله : (ولا إيلاء فيما دون أربعة أشهر) يعني في الحرة بدليل أنه سيذكر حكم الأمة وبه قال الأئمة الأربعة وظاهر الآية صحة الإيلاء فيما دونها لأنه إنما خص بالأربعة مدة التربص وأما الحلف فمطلق، وما ذكره الشارح وغيره من المعنى فمصادرة كما في فتح القدير ولكن كان مشايخنا إنما تمسكوا بفتوى ابن عباس على أنه تفسير للآية وتمامه في العناية والله أعلم
He said: (And there is no ila' in less than four months) meaning regarding a free woman, as evidence that he will mention the ruling of a slave woman. And the four imams agreed with this. The apparent meaning of the verse (supports) the validity of ila' for less than that because He only specified four months for the period of waiting, while the oath is absolute. The meaning mentioned by the commentator and others is circular reasoning as in Fath al-Qadir, but our scholars only adhered to the fatwa of Ibn Abbas as an interpretation of the verse. The completion is in al-Inaya, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe (sharh) on the matn statement 'There is no ila' in less than four months.' The commentator clarifies that this ruling applies specifically to free women, as the ruling for slave women will be mentioned separately. He notes that all four imams agree on this ruling. The commentator then addresses a potential objection: the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse (Surah al-Baqarah 2:226) seems to allow ila' for any duration, because the verse imposes a four-month waiting period after an oath, but does not specify a minimum oath duration. The commentator refutes the alternative reasoning as circular (مصادرة), citing Fath al-Qadir. The relied-upon proof is the fatwa of Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him), which interprets the verse as requiring a minimum of four months. This fatwa is considered a definitive interpretation (tafsir) of the verse, not an addition to the text. The commentator directs to al-Inaya for the complete discussion.

Key Terms
إيلاء (ila'): An oath by a husband to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for a specified period.
تربص (tarabbus): The waiting period of four months after which the wife may seek judicial separation if the husband does not resume relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One month
B) Four months
C) Two months
D) One year

Key Takeaway
Ila' requires an oath of at least four months for free women; this ruling is based on the fatwa of Ibn Abbas as an interpretation of Quran 2:226.

Talaq — Divorce

Multiple Oaths: Combining vs Repeating Negation and Oath
Commentary on combining and repeating oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between an oath combined with 'and' and an oath repeated in wording, and state the number of expiations owed in each case.

Core Idea
Repeating the negation or the oath creates multiple oaths; merely combining with 'and' does not.

The passage begins by clarifying a key distinction: when a husband says 'I will not approach you for two months and two months', it counts as a single ila' oath. But if he repeats the negation (e.g., 'nor' clauses) or repeats the entire oath formula, it becomes two separate oaths, each with its own period and expiation requirement. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its legal effects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the husband's statement 'by Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months' is one ila' oath, as combining with 'and' is like repeating the same wording.
2
Distinguish repetition patterns
Compare the above with repeating the negation (e.g., 'by Allah, not two months nor two months') or repeating the entire oath (e.g., 'by Allah, not two months; by Allah, not two months'). In both cases, it becomes two separate oaths.
Even repeating only the name of Allah (e.g., 'by Allah, by Allah') counts as two oaths in zahir al-riwayah.
3
Apply the ruling on expiations
For repeated oaths, the periods overlap. If he approaches before the shorter period ends, two expiations are owed (one for each oath). If he approaches after both periods expire, no expiation is owed.
4
Note the generalization
The ruling of an ordinary oath (yamin) is the same as ila' in this regard: not multiple if only with 'and', multiple if the negation or oath is repeated.
This establishes a consistent rule for all oaths.

He said: (And by Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months is ila') because combining with the conjunction 'and' is like combining with the word itself. His saying 'after these two months' is an incidental qualification because if he had not mentioned it, the ruling would be the same. It is qualified with 'and' without repeating the negation and the oath because if he repeated the negation by saying 'by Allah, I will not approach you for two months nor for two months' or repeated the oath by saying 'by Allah, I will not approach you for two months, by Allah, I will not approach you for two months', it would not be ila' because they are two oaths, so their periods overlap. If he approaches her before two months pass, two expiations are required; if he approaches after they pass, no expiation is required because the periods have expired. The ruling of an oath is like the ruling of ila' in not being multiple if only with 'and', and multiplicity if the negation or the oath is repeated. There is no difference in repeating the oath whether the object of the oath is repeated or not, even if he says 'by Allah, by Allah, I will not do such-and-such', it is two oaths in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), like his saying 'by Allah, I will not do such-and-such, by Allah, I will not do such-and-such'. Know that there is no necessary correlation between being ila' and being an oath; thus, sometimes the fulfillment (birr) and violation (hanth) may be multiple or single, or the fulfillment may be multiple and the violation single, and vice versa. The first example: If he says 'if tomorrow comes, by Allah, I will not approach you; if the day after tomorrow comes, by Allah, I will not approach you', then ila' is multiple due to multiple periods, and the oath is multiple due to multiple mention. If he abstains for four months from the first day, he fulfills the first and she is divorced; then if another day passes, he fulfills the second and she is also divorced. If he approaches her after the day after tomorrow, two expiations are required; if he approaches her on the coming tomorrow, one expiation is required. Second example: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months' and likewise the book's case. His saying: (Circular reasoning as in Fath al-Qadir, its text: 'The meaning mentioned is that the mu'li (one who takes the oath) is someone who cannot approach within the period except by something that is required of him, but this is not the case; it is based on the minimum period being four months, otherwise we do not say that, since we said there is no restriction of the period sworn upon by it. So establishing the minimum as four months by this is circular reasoning.') In al-Inaya he said: 'If it is said: The fatwa of Ibn Abbas contradicts the apparent meaning of the text because Allah Almighty said: "For those who swear off their wives, a waiting period of four months" [2:226]. He used ila' absolutely and restricted the waiting period to a term. This implies that whoever swears off his wife, even for a short period like a day or an hour, must wait four months. Restricting the oath to a period would be an addition to the text, which is not permissible by the fatwa of Ibn Abbas. The answer is that the fatwa of Ibn [page break] ila' and if he stays a day then said 'by Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months' or said 'by Allah, I will not approach you for a year except a day' or said 'in Basra, by Allah, I will not enter Mecca' while she is there, it is not [ila']? No, it is not ila' in these three cases. The third example: 'Whenever you enter this house, by Allah, I will not approach you' and she entered it on a day, then on another day, then on another day; if he approaches her, one expiation is required due to unity of violation; if he abstains from her for four months from the first day, she is divorced by one divorce; if another day passes, she is divorced by another divorce; similarly if another day passes, she is divorced by a third divorce due to multiplicity of fulfillment. In Fath al-Qadir: 'There is a problem in this example because the oath by Allah occurs as the penalty for a repeated condition, so it must be repeated. It is not problematic that there is no oath at the second and third condition because the name of Allah Almighty is not mentioned therein; otherwise, it would follow that there is no oath at the first condition either, yet the oath is established there. Perhaps it was confused with 'by Allah, whenever you enter the house, I will not approach you' or with 'whenever you enter the house, by Allah, I will not approach you'. The answer: There is no confusion because what is transmitted in the fatwa collections like al-Walwaljiyya and al-Bazzaziyya is that divorce, manumission, and zihar, whenever suspended on a repeated condition, are repeated, but the oath is not, even if suspended on a repeated condition. So if he says 'Whenever you enter the house, by Allah, I will not speak to Zayd' and she enters the house multiple times, the oath is not repeated because it is the creation of a contract, and creation is not repeated without repetition of its formula. Do you not see that it is not repeated even if multiplicity is specified because expiation is not required without violating the sanctity of the name of Allah? And his saying that the implication is that there is no oath at the first condition is rejected because it is explicitly conditional, as is not hidden. The fourth example, namely the unity of ila' and multiplicity of the oath: If he says 'if tomorrow comes, by Allah, I will not approach you' then he says in the session 'if tomorrow comes, by Allah, I will not approach you', it is one ila' in the ruling of fulfillment, so if four months of the tomorrow pass, she is divorced; if he approaches her, he owes two expiations due to unity of period and multiplicity of the name.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This is an expansion probe (sharh) on the rules of multiple oaths and their relation to ila'. The passage begins by explaining that an oath combining two periods with 'and' (e.g., 'two months and two months') is considered one ila' oath. However, if the negation or the oath itself is repeated (e.g., 'by Allah, not two months nor two months' or repeating the full oath), it becomes two separate oaths, and the legal effects differ: he may owe multiple expiations. The commentator then establishes a general rule: there is no necessary correlation (la talazum) between being an ila' oath and being an ordinary oath. This means that the number of ila' oaths (which affect divorce) and the number of ordinary oaths (which affect expiation) can differ. He provides four examples to illustrate various combinations. The first example shows multiple ila' and multiple oaths. The second example shows the book's case. The third example involves a conditional oath repeated upon entry; there is a dispute with Fath al-Qadir about whether the oath repeats. The Hanafi position, based on fatwa collections, is that the oath itself does not repeat because it is an instant contract, unlike the suspended rulings (divorce, etc.). The fourth example shows unity of ila' but multiplicity of oaths. The passage also includes a digression refuting the claim that the four-month minimum is circular reasoning, citing Fath al-Qadir and al-Inaya, and affirming the fatwa of Ibn Abbas as the basis. The final part discusses cases where ila' does not occur: if he stays a day and then takes a new oath for two months after the first two months, or for a year except a day, or an oath not to enter Mecca while she is there, these are not ila'.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): An oath taken by a husband, which may or may not constitute ila' depending on the duration and wording.
إيلاء (ila'): A special oath where a husband swears not to approach his wife for four months or more, leading to divorce by court decree if he does not resume relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'By Allah, I will not speak to you for a week and a week', how many expiations are owed if he speaks within the first week?
A) One expiation
B) Two expiations
C) No expiation
D) Four expiations

Key Takeaway
The number of oaths is determined by the wording pattern: combining with 'and' yields one oath, while repeating the negation or the oath yields multiple oaths.

Talaq — Divorce
