The Hanafi Position on Khul' as a Bain Divorce and the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Proving with hadith that khul' is a bain divorce and refuting opposing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khul' as a bain divorce, cite the primary hadith evidence, and explain the practical consequence of the disagreement with the Hanbali school.

Core Idea
Khul' is a bain divorce, not an annulment: the hadith 'al-khul'u tatliqatun bā'inah' settles it.

Khul' (divorce by compensation) is a well-known means of marital dissolution, but its legal classification varies among madhhabs. This passage presents the Hanafi proof that it is a bain divorce, rebuts the Hanbali view of annulment, and clarifies the authority of judges in such matters.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that khul' results in a bain (irrevocable) divorce based on the explicit hadith.
The hadith is directly quoted: 'al-khul'u tatliqatun bā'inah'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that the Hanbali school considers khul' a faskh (annulment) that does not count as divorce.
Some others also hold it as a raj'i divorce, but the main opposing view is the Hanbali position.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand that the Hanbalis argue that since khul' involves compensation and does not reduce the number of divorces, it is an annulment.
They also rely on the principle that divorce is a unilateral right of the husband.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith is explicit and that the word khul' is a kinayah meaning divorce, so compensation does not change its nature.
The Hanafis also argue that the hadith is clear enough to override qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If khul' is a divorce, it counts toward the three divorces and the wife becomes bain. If it is faskh, it does not count and the couple can remarry without tahleel.
This practical difference affects subsequent marriage rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: What occurs by it and by divorce for wealth is a bain divorce, i.e., by legal khul'. As for khul', due to his statement, peace be upon him, 'Khul' is a bain divorce' and because it is probable to be divorce so it became among the kinayah, and what occurs by kinayah is bain. And in al-Khulasa: If a judge ruled that it is an annulment, it is said it is executed and it is said it is not. The first is apparent because he ruled in a disputed matter, and our school is the opinion of the majority. Among scholars are those who say it is not permissible at all, and among them are those who restrict it to the case where she hates him and fears not fulfilling her rights or his rights, and among them are those who say it is not permissible except with the ruler's permission. The Hanbalis said: No divorce occurs by it; rather it is an annulment, on condition that he does not intend divorce, so it does not reduce the number of divorces. Some said: Raj'i divorce occurs, and if he returns to her, he returns the compensation he took. The completion is in Fath al-Qadeer. He made it absolute so it includes cases without compensation also, and when it occurs with the word khul' or bay' or mubara'ah, and when he does not intend divorce by it but with the condition of mentioning compensation, so if he says 'I did not intend divorce' while mentioning it, he is not believed judicially but is believed in conscience because Allah knows what is in his heart, but it is not permissible for the woman to remain with him because she, like the judge, only knows the apparent. This is in al-Mabsut. And the condition of mentioning divorce is like intention, as in al-Khaniya. His statement: It is said it is executed and it is said it is not) Al-Shurunbulali said: The judges of this time have no option but to judge by the sound opinion of the school, which is that it is bain. It was mentioned in Hashiyat Miskin from the introduction of al-Durr al-Mukhtar quoting from Shaykh Qasim in his verification that ruling and issuing fatwa with the weaker opinion is ignorance and a breach of consensus, and that the disagreement is specific to the mujtahid judge. As for the muqallid, his judgment contrary to his school is not executed at all, as in al-Quniya. Especially in our time, the sultan in his manifesto forbids ruling with weak opinions, so how about contrary to his school? So he is dismissed with respect to non-reliable opinions in his school, and his ruling is not executed and is overturned. This is detailed in the chapter of qada' in al-Fath, al-Bahr, and al-Nahr. So what is in al-Bahr here from his statement 'the apparent is execution' is contrary to the relied-upon opinion. And it is not hidden what is in it, for the author's intention is that if a judge who considers it an annulment, like a Hanbali, rules accordingly, his ruling is executed because it is a matter of ijtihad that does not contradict a clear text, and if it is raised to a Hanafi, he upholds it. But if it is one of the mentioned cases, he overturns it due to lack of execution of the ruling, as will be explained in its place.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a dispute over whether khul' is a divorce or an annulment. The Hanafi position is that khul' is a bain divorce, based on the hadith 'al-khul'u tatliqatun bā'inah' and because the word khul' is a kinayah that bears the meaning of divorce. The Hanbalis hold it is an annulment (faskh) that does not count as divorce, while some others say it is a raj'i revocable divorce. The text also discusses the authority of a judge in this matter: if a judge rules it is an annulment, his ruling may be executed if he is a mujtahid, but for a muqallid judge, his ruling contrary to his school is invalid. The relied-upon position for fatwa and judging is that khul' is bain.

Key Terms
البائن (al-bā'in): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; the husband cannot return to her without a new marriage.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Annulment that dissolves the marriage without counting as a divorce.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce by compensation initiated by the wife's offer.
الكناية (al-kināyah): An indirect expression that can imply divorce but is not explicit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Rulings on Claims (Da'wa) in Khul': Whose Word is Accepted
Presenting the Hanafi rule that the husband's claim about the nature of the payment is accepted in khul' disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whose statement is accepted in disputes over khul' compensation and apply the underlying principle to new scenarios.

Core Idea
In khul' payment disputes, the husband's word is accepted because he denies an obligation and admits only one debt.

When a marriage ends by khul', the wife often pays compensation (badal) to the husband. Disputes can arise whether money already handed over was part of the khul' agreement or a separate debt. The Hanafi school has a clear procedural rule to resolve such disagreements, based on who is denying what obligation. This lesson unpacks that rule from the authoritative text of al-Bazzaziyya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The husband claims an exception (istithna) or condition in the khul' agreement, effectively saying the payment was for a different reason (e.g., a debt). The wife claims it was khul' compensation.
2
Determine the defendant
The husband is denying that the payment was khul' compensation, so he is the defendant regarding that obligation. The wife is the plaintiff claiming compensation.
In Hanafi evidence law, the defendant's statement with an oath is preferred.
3
Apply the principle
Since the husband denies the obligation of compensation, his statement is taken. He admits only one debt (the original loan), while the wife claims two debts (loan + compensation).
The passage states: 'فالقول له لأنه أنكر وجوب البدل عليها وأقر أن له عليها مالاً واحداً لا مالين'
4
Note the exception
If there is evidence that the husband explicitly undertook (التزام البدل) or received the payment as khul' compensation, then the wife's claim may be accepted, because the fatwa is on the validity of the changer and invalidator except when such evidence appears.
The text says: 'والفتوى على صحة دعوى المغير والمبطل إلا إذا ظهر ما ذكرنا من التزام البدل أو قبضه'
5
Compare with other scenarios
If the husband claims only revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) without any compensation, no money is due and his statement stands. If he divorces her for a payment and then makes khul', the khul' is invalid because she is already bain.
These are distinct cases that reinforce the general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البزازية ادعى الاستثناء أو الشرط في الخلع وكذبته فيه فالقول له إلى أن قال: والفتوى على صحة دعوى المغير والمبطل إلا إذا ظهر ما ذكرنا من التزام البدل أو قبضه أو نحوه ادعى الاستثناء وقال قبضت ما قبضت منك بحق لي عليك وقالت بل لبدل الخلع فالقول له لأنه أنكر وجوب البدل عليها وأقر أن له عليها مالاً واحداً لا مالين والمرأة مقرة أن له عليها مالاً آخر فيكون القول له بخلاف ما إذا لم يدع بالطلاق الرجعي فقط لعدم لزوم المال والرجعي يلحق البائن بخلاف ما إذا طلقها بمال ثم خلعها فإنه يلزم المال ولا يصح الخلع لأنها بانت منه بالطلاق
And in al-Bazzaziyya: If he claimed an exception or condition in khul' and she denied him, then the statement is his. Up to he said: And the fatwa is on the validity of the claim of the changer and the invalidator unless what we mentioned of the undertaking of the compensation or its receipt or the like appears. He claimed an exception and said: I took what I took from you as a right due to me upon you, and she said: Rather it is for the compensation of khul', then the statement is his because he denies that the compensation is obligatory upon her and affirms that he has one debt upon her, not two debts, while the wife affirms that he has another debt upon her, so the statement is his. Unlike when he did not claim the revocable divorce only, due to the absence of obligation of wealth, and the revocable attaches to the bain. Unlike when he divorces her for wealth then makes khul' with her, for the wealth is obligatory and the khul' is not valid because she has become bain from him by the divorce.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on judicial claims in khul' cases. When a husband and wife dispute whether money paid was khul' compensation or a separate debt, the husband's claim is accepted because he is denying an obligation on her (khul' compensation) and admitting to one debt, while she is claiming two debts. The general principle in Hanafi fiqh is that the defendant's statement with an oath is accepted over the plaintiff's claim. Here, the husband is considered the defendant regarding the khul' compensation, so his statement is taken. The passage also notes exceptions and compares with the case of revocable divorce.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithnā'): An exception or stipulation made by the husband in the khul' agreement that affects the nature of the payment
البدل (al-badal): The compensation paid by the wife in khul'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wife's
B) The husband's
C) Both are believed equally
D) A judge decides arbitrarily

Key Takeaway
In khul' disputes over the nature of payment, the husband's statement is accepted because he denies the obligation, unless there is evidence of an explicit undertaking or receipt of compensation.

Invalidity of Khul' After Bain Talaq and Apostasy
States invalidity of khul' after bain talaq and apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that khul' after bain talaq or apostasy is invalid and explain the consequences regarding the mahr and wilayat al-jabr.

Core Idea
Khul' requires an existing marriage; after bain divorce or apostasy, no marriage remains to dissolve.

Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. However, khul' presupposes that the marriage is still intact. If the husband has already given an irrevocable (bain) divorce, the marriage is already dissolved, so khul' has no effect. Similarly, apostasy nullifies the marriage, so khul' after apostasy is also invalid. This lesson clarifies the ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Context
Recognize that the ruling concerns khul' (wife-initiated divorce) performed after either a bain talaq (irrevocable divorce) or apostasy by one spouse.
2
Understand the Reasoning
Khul' is only valid when the marriage is still in existence. A bain talaq dissolves the marriage irrevocably, and apostasy also dissolves the marriage (or suspends it until repentance). Thus, after either event, there is no marital bond left for khul' to operate on.
In apostasy, the marriage is suspended; if the apostate returns within the iddah, the marriage revives. However, khul' during the suspension is ineffective because the marriage is not fully intact.
3
Learn the Consequences
If khul' is performed after bain talaq or apostasy, it is invalid. The mahr (dower) does not fall; it remains owed by the husband (if already paid, it is not returned). In the case of apostasy, the husband retains wilayat al-jabr (authority to compel) over the marriage, meaning he can take the wife back if she returns to Islam.
Wilayat al-jabr applies only in apostasy, not after bain talaq, because bain talaq ends the marriage completely.
4
Memorize the Ruling
Commit to memory: Khul' after bain talaq or apostasy is invalid (batil). The mahr does not fall, and in apostasy the husband retains wilayat al-jabr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخرج الخلع بعد الطلاق البائن وبعد الردة فإنه غير صحيح فيهما فلا يسقط المهر ويبقى له بعد الخلع ولاية الجبر على النكاح في الردة كما في البزازية .
And khul' after the irrevocable divorce (bain talaq) and after apostasy: it is not valid in both cases, so the dower (mahr) does not fall, and he retains after khul' the authority of coercion (wilayat al-jabr) over marriage in the case of apostasy, as mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the sharh. It clarifies that khul' is only valid if the marriage is still in existence. If the husband has already given a bain divorce (irrevocable) or if the wife has apostatized, then performing khul' has no effect. In the case of apostasy, the husband retains wilayat al-jabr (authority to compel) over the marriage, meaning he can take her back if she returns to Islam, as per al-Bazzaziyya.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (fidyah) to the husband.
الطلاق البائن (al-talaq al-bain): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately without the possibility of revocation (raj'ah).
ولاية الجبر (wilayat al-jabr): The authority of the husband to compel the wife to return to the marriage in certain circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, is khul' valid after the husband gives a bain divorce?
A) Yes, it is valid and the mahr falls.
B) No, it is not valid and the mahr does not fall.
C) Yes, but only if the woman apostatizes.
D) No, but the mahr falls anyway.

Key Takeaway
Khul' is invalid after bain talaq or apostasy because the marriage is no longer intact; the mahr remains due and the husband retains wilayat al-jabr in the case of apostasy.

Khul' as an Irrevocable Divorce: The Hanafi View
Explains the Hanafi view that khul' is a bain divorce using hadith and analogy to kinayat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school considers khul' a bain divorce and derive the ruling from the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Khul' is a bain divorce because the hadith explicitly says so and because it functions as a kinayah for talaq.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation) results in an irrevocable bain divorce. We will examine the primary textual evidence and the reasoning that classifies it as a type of talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
The passage states that valid khul' produces a bain (irrevocable) divorce. Note the phrase 'طلاق بائن' and that it applies 'بالخلع الشرعي' (by valid khul').
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah: 'الخلع تطليقة بائنة' (Khul' is an irrevocable divorce). This is the central proof.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'تطليقة' explicitly classifies khul' as a type of talaq (divorce), and 'بائنة' indicates irrevocability. Thus the hadith directly supports the Hanafi view.
4
Note the secondary reasoning (kinayah)
The commentator adds that khul' has become a kinayah (indirect expression) for talaq, and in Hanafi fiqh, a divorce via kinayah is bain. This reinforces the ruling.
5
Acknowledge authority level
This is the mufta bihi (operative) position in the Hanafi school, based on zahir al-riwayah and supported by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال من قوله : الواقع به وبالطلاق على مال طلاق بائن أي بالخلع الشرعي، أما الخلع فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الخلع تطليقة بائنة ولأنه يحتمل الطلاق حتى صار من الكنايات والواقع بالكناية بائن. وفي الخلاصة : ولو قضى بكون الخلع فسخاً قيل ينفذ وقيل لا اهـ. والظاهر الأول لأنه قضى في فصل مجتهد فيه ومذهبنا قول الجمهور، ومن العلماء بعدم مشروعيته أصلاً، ومنهم من قيده بما إذا كرهته وخاف أن لا يوفيها حقها وأن لا توفيه، ومنهم من قال لا يجوز إلا بإذن السلطان. وقالت الحنابلة : لا يقع به طلاق بل هو فسخ بشرط عدم نية الطلاق فلا ينقص العدد وقال قوم وقع به رجعي فإن راجعها رد البدل الذي أخذه وتمامه في فتح القدير .
He said from his statement: 'That which occurs by it and by talaq in exchange for property is an irrevocable divorce (bain)' meaning by the valid khul'. As for khul', it is due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Khul' is an irrevocable divorce' and because it is probable of talaq such that it became from the indirect expressions (kinayat), and that which occurs by kinaya is bain. In al-Khulasa: 'If a judge ruled that khul' is a dissolution (faskh), it is said it is enforceable and it is said it is not.' The first is apparent because he ruled in a discretionary matter (mujtahad fihi) and our school is the view of the majority. And among scholars are those who deem it impermissible completely, and among them are those who restrict it to when she dislikes him and fears not fulfilling her rights, and among them are those who say it is not allowed except with the permission of the ruler. The Hanbalis said: 'No talaq occurs by it; rather it is a dissolution (faskh) on condition of not intending talaq, so it does not reduce the count.' And some said: 'It is a revocable divorce (raj'i); if he takes her back, he returns the compensation he took.' And its completion is in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling that khul' results in a bain divorce. The commentator first explains that the phrase in the matn 'الواقع به وبالطلاق على مال طلاق بائن' means a bain divorce through valid khul'. He then provides the primary proof: the hadith 'الخلع تطليقة بائنة' (khul' is an irrevocable divorce). He also notes that khul' has become a kinayah (indirect expression) for talaq, and a divorce via kinayah is bain. Then he discusses a disagreement: if a judge from another school (e.g., Hanbali) rules that khul' is a faskh (dissolution), is that judgment enforceable? There are two opinions: the preferred one (zahir) is that it is enforceable because it is a matter of ijtihad. Then he lists various positions of other schools: some reject khul' entirely, some restrict it to cases of mutual dislike, some require ruler's permission. The Hanbalis consider it a faskh, not talaq, so it doesn't reduce the count of divorces. Another group considers it a raj'i divorce, requiring return of compensation upon revocation. The text ends by referring to Fath al-Qadir for more detail.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by wife in exchange for compensation.
تطليقة بائنة (tallaqa bā'ina): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, after which the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage contract.
كنايات (kināyāt): Indirect expressions that imply divorce but require intention to effect divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Scholarly Disagreements on Khul' and Their Implications
Enumerates various scholarly positions on khul' and discusses the enforceability of a judge's ruling that differs from the Hanafi view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the various positions on khul' among different schools and explain the Hanafi view on the enforceability of a judge's ruling that diverges from it.

Core Idea
The nature of khul' (bain/faskh/raj'i) is disputed; Hanafi considers it bain, but a judge's ijtihad can be enforced within the mufta bihi framework.

While the Hanafi school firmly holds that khul' is a bain divorce, other scholars have taken different positions: some reject it entirely, some restrict it, and the Hanbalis consider it a faskh. This lesson surveys these differing views and examines the question of whether a judge's ruling based on a non-Hanafi view is enforceable within the Hanafi legal system.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi position (review)
Recall from the previous lesson that Hanafi holds khul' as a bain talaq based on explicit hadith and kinayah.
This is the baseline.
2
Survey the other positions on khul'
The passage lists: (1) some scholars reject khul' entirely; (2) some restrict it to cases of mutual dislike and fear of failing marital duties; (3) some require the ruler's permission; (4) Hanbalis say it is faskh, not talaq, so it doesn't reduce the count; (5) some say it is raj'i, with return of compensation upon revocation.
Note the variety: each has its own evidence.
3
Identify the Hanafi legal response to conflicting qada'
The passage addresses: if a judge rules that khul' is faskh, is his judgment enforceable? Two opinions: 'it is said enforceable, and it is said not.' The preferred view (zahir) is that it is enforceable because the matter is open to ijtihad.
This shows the flexibility within Hanafi legal theory.
4
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference between the views: if khul' is bain, it uses one of three divorces; if faskh, it does not; if raj'i, revocation is allowed during idda.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال من قوله : الواقع به وبالطلاق على مال طلاق بائن أي بالخلع الشرعي، أما الخلع فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الخلع تطليقة بائنة ولأنه يحتمل الطلاق حتى صار من الكنايات والواقع بالكناية بائن. وفي الخلاصة : ولو قضى بكون الخلع فسخاً قيل ينفذ وقيل لا اهـ. والظاهر الأول لأنه قضى في فصل مجتهد فيه ومذهبنا قول الجمهور، ومن العلماء بعدم مشروعيته أصلاً، ومنهم من قيده بما إذا كرهته وخاف أن لا يوفيها حقها وأن لا توفيه، ومنهم من قال لا يجوز إلا بإذن السلطان. وقالت الحنابلة : لا يقع به طلاق بل هو فسخ بشرط عدم نية الطلاق فلا ينقص العدد وقال قوم وقع به رجعي فإن راجعها رد البدل الذي أخذه وتمامه في فتح القدير .
He said from his statement: 'That which occurs by it and by talaq in exchange for property is an irrevocable divorce (bain)' meaning by the valid khul'. As for khul', it is due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Khul' is an irrevocable divorce' and because it is probable of talaq such that it became from the indirect expressions (kinayat), and that which occurs by kinaya is bain. In al-Khulasa: 'If a judge ruled that khul' is a dissolution (faskh), it is said it is enforceable and it is said it is not.' The first is apparent because he ruled in a discretionary matter (mujtahad fihi) and our school is the view of the majority. And among scholars are those who deem it impermissible completely, and among them are those who restrict it to when she dislikes him and fears not fulfilling her rights, and among them are those who say it is not allowed except with the permission of the ruler. The Hanbalis said: 'No talaq occurs by it; rather it is a dissolution (faskh) on condition of not intending talaq, so it does not reduce the count.' And some said: 'It is a revocable divorce (raj'i); if he takes her back, he returns the compensation he took.' And its completion is in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling that khul' results in a bain divorce. The commentator first explains that the phrase in the matn 'الواقع به وبالطلاق على مال طلاق بائن' means a bain divorce through valid khul'. He then provides the primary proof: the hadith 'الخلع تطليقة بائنة' (khul' is an irrevocable divorce). He also notes that khul' has become a kinayah (indirect expression) for talaq, and a divorce via kinayah is bain. Then he discusses a disagreement: if a judge from another school (e.g., Hanbali) rules that khul' is a faskh (dissolution), is that judgment enforceable? There are two opinions: the preferred one (zahir) is that it is enforceable because it is a matter of ijtihad. Then he lists various positions of other schools: some reject khul' entirely, some restrict it to cases of mutual dislike, some require ruler's permission. The Hanbalis consider it a faskh, not talaq, so it doesn't reduce the count of divorces. Another group considers it a raj'i divorce, requiring return of compensation upon revocation. The text ends by referring to Fath al-Qadir for more detail.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by wife in exchange for compensation.
فسخ (faskh): Dissolution of the marriage contract, not considered a divorce; does not reduce the number of divorces.
رجعي (raj'ī): A revocable divorce where the husband can take the wife back during the waiting period without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred Hanafi view on whether a judge's ruling that khul' is faskh is enforceable?
A) It is not enforceable because it contradicts the Hanafi school.
B) It is enforceable because it is a matter of ijtihad.
C) It is enforceable only if the judge is a Hanafi.
D) It is not enforceable unless the couple agrees.

Key Takeaway
Khul' is subject to significant ikhtilaf; the Hanafi school holds it as bain talaq, but respects the enforceability of differing judicial rulings in matters of ijtihad.

The Generality of Khul' and the Role of Intention
Opens the discussion on khul' generality and intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the generality of khul' and distinguish between the evidentiary value of the husband's denial of intention in qada' versus diyana.

Core Idea
Khul' is valid with or without compensation; the husband's denial of intention is accepted only before Allah, not in court.

In this passage, the commentator establishes that khul' (divorce by redemption) is general: it applies whether or not compensation (iwad) is mentioned, and with various wordings. He then addresses a key issue: if the husband claims he did not intend divorce despite mentioning compensation, his word is not accepted in court (qada') but he may be truthful before Allah (diyana). This distinction between apparent evidence and inner truth is fundamental to Hanafi fiqh, and it sets the stage for understanding how such claims are handled in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of khul'
The passage begins with 'Aṭlaqahu fa-shamila' — he made it general, so it includes when there is no compensation, and when the wording is khul', bay' (sale), or mubara'ah. Confirm that the ruling applies broadly.
Generality is key: khul' is not restricted to cases with compensation or specific wording.
2
Analyze the husband's denial of intention
If the husband mentions compensation but says 'I did not intend divorce', he is not believed in qada' (judicially) but is believed in diyana (before Allah). Understand why: the court relies on apparent evidence (the mention of compensation indicates intention), but Allah knows the inner truth.
The woman cannot live with him because the apparent evidence supports divorce.
3
Understand the role of discussing divorce
The state of discussing divorce (mudhākarat al-ṭalāq) is considered equivalent to intention (niyya) for indirect expressions (kināyāt). This means that if a husband utters a kināyah word in the context of discussing divorce, it effects a divorce without separate intention.
This is a Hanafi principle: context can substitute for explicit intention.

He made it general, so it includes when it is without compensation also, and when it occurs with the word khul', sale (bay'), or barā'a, and when he did not intend talaq by it but on condition of mentioning the compensation, such that if he said 'I did not intend talaq' along with mentioning it, he is not believed in qada (judicially) but is believed in diyana (before Allah), because Allah knows what is in his secret, but the woman cannot live with him because she, like the judge, only knows the apparent. Thus is it in al-Mabsut. And the state of discussing talaq is like intention (niyya) as in al-Khaniyya. And in al-Bazzaziyya: if he claims an exception (istithnā) or condition (shart) in khul' and she denies him, then the statement is his (qawl lahu) until he says: and the fatwa is on the validity of the claim of the changer and invalidator, except if what we mentioned of the undertaking of the payment or its receipt or similar appears. He claimed an exception and said: I took what I took from you as a right you owed me, and she said: Rather it is for the khul' payment, then the statement is his because he denied the obligation of the payment upon her and affirmed that she owes him one property, not two, and the woman confirms that she owes him another property, so the statement is his, contrary to if he did not claim... For revocable divorce only because no property is binding, and the revocable attaches to the irrevocable, contrary to if he divorced her for property then performed khul' with her, then the property is binding and the khul' is not valid because she has become irrevocably separated from him by the divorce. He said: ('It is said it is enforceable and it is said it is not'). Al-Shurnublaliyya said: The judges of this time have no choice but to judge by the soundest (asahh) of the madhhab, which is that it is bain. Said in Hashiyat Miskin: and mentioned in the introduction of al-Durr al-Mukhtar, quoting from Shaykh Qasim in his correction, that ruling and giving fatwa by the weak opinion (marjuh) is ignorance and violates consensus, and that disagreement is specific to the mujtahid judge; as for the muqallid, his judgment contrary to his madhhab is not enforceable at all, as in al-Quniyya, especially in our time; the ruler stipulates in his decree the prohibition of judging by weak sayings, so how about contrary to his madhhab? So he is dismissed regarding non-reliant parts of his madhhab, so his judgment is not enforceable and is annulled, as expanded in Qada' al-Fath, al-Bahr, and al-Nahr. So what is in al-Bahr here from his saying 'the apparent is enforceability' is contrary to the relied-upon. It is not hidden what is in it, for the intention of the author is that if a judge ruled that it is a dissolution (faskh) like a Hanbali, his judgment is enforceable because it is in a discretionary matter that does not oppose a clear book, a well-known sunna, or consensus. And if it is raised to a Hanafi, he enforces it. But if it is one of what was mentioned, he annuls it due to lack of enforceability, as will come in its place. He said: ('Claimed exception etc.') This is like an exception from his saying 'except if what appeared...' The exception because he claims upon her the khul' payment and she denies, so the statement is hers. And if the payment is not mentioned, it is from the indirect expressions (kinayat), so it is dependent on intention or discussion of talaq if it is with the word khul' or barā'a, and if with the word bay' (sale) like 'I sold you yourself' or 'your talaq', then no, because it contradicts the apparent. And he has benefited that the occurrence of the bain divorce and its rule will come later in its description: that it is an oath from his side and a contract from her side, so he cannot revoke it, and it is not invalidated by his leaving the session, and it is valid if appended from him, and the rules are reversed regarding her if she starts, as will come. And he did not mention its condition because its condition is the condition of talaq, but acceptance from her is necessary when it is for compensation or with the word khala'tuk or ikhtali'i. Hence in al-Muhit: if he said 'ikhtali'i' and she said 'ikhtala'tu', she is divorced and the mahr falls, because his saying 'ikhtali'i' is an order for talaq with the word khul', and the woman owns talaq by the husband's order, so it becomes like him saying 'tallaqi nafsiki talaqan bā'inan'. Contrary to his saying 'ishtari nafsaki minni' and she said 'ishtaraytu', she is not divorced until the husband says 'bi'tu' because it is an order for khul' which is a contract because the sale is a contract... if the consideration is not mentioned and known, it is not valid. And if he mentions an unknown consideration, such as if he said 'ikhlai' nafsaki bi māl' and she said 'ikhtala'tu nafsi bi alf dirham', the khul' is not complete and she is not divorced until the husband says 'khala'tu' because the delegation of khul' to her is not valid because when he mentioned the consideration, it is in fact a khul', and khul' is not valid without specifying the consideration, and the consideration here is unknown, so it is not valid. And if he mentions a known consideration, such as saying 'ikhlai' nafsaki bi alf dirham' and she says 'ikhtala'tu bi alf dirham', it is a contract... we mentioned and the summary is that his claim of exception is accepted except if he mentioned the consideration in the khul' contract, because the explicit mention of the consideration is an indication of the intention of khul', so he is not believed in his claim to invalidate it by the exception, except if he claims that what he took is not the khul' payment but another right, like a debt or deposit, then his claim of exception is accepted due to the lack of indication... because if his statement is accepted regarding what he took, the khul' with payment does not remain. But there is that the indication of the intention of khul' is the mention of the consideration in the khul', not its receipt afterwards. So if he mentions the consideration, then takes money from her, then claims exception and claims that what he took is another right besides the consideration, the indication of the intention of khul' is not removed, so his claim of exception is not valid and the khul' contract with consideration remains, so his claim that what he took is another right is not accepted because when the consideration remains, the statement is the woman's that what she paid is the khul' payment, not other, because the statement is of the one who conveys (al-mumallik). Thus there is no difference between claiming exception and not, as the statement is the woman's in both cases. What the author mentioned is verbatim in Jami' al-Fusulayn, but he said at its end 'there is consideration' and did not explain its reason. Perhaps what we mentioned is the intention of the author of al-Fusulayn by 'consideration'. And Allah knows best. He said: ('Contrary to if he did not claim the exception') mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya after his saying 'the statement is hers' as text: 'She paid the khul' payment and the husband disputed that he took it in another capacity. Imam Zahir al-Din gave a fatwa that the statement is his, and it is said hers because she is the one who conveyed (al-mumallika).' He said: ('It is dependent on intention or discussion of talaq') Will come at his saying 'and khul' and mubara'a are annulled' that the mashayikh did not require intention in khul' because of the predominance of usage and because it usually occurs after discussion of talaq. So consider.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This lengthy passage covers multiple aspects of khul'. First, the commentator states that the ruling of khul' being bain is general, applying whether or not compensation is mentioned, and with various wordings (khul', bay', mubara'a). However, if compensation is mentioned, the husband's denial of intention for divorce is not accepted in court (qada') but may be true before Allah (diyana). The wife cannot remain with him due to apparent evidence. Then it discusses the rule that discussion of talaq (mudhakara al-talaq) is equivalent to intention for kinayat. Next, it addresses the issue of istithna' (exception): if the husband claims that the compensation he received was not for khul' but for another right, and the wife disputes, his statement is generally accepted (qawluhu) except when the compensation is explicitly mentioned in the contract, which indicates intention for khul'. Then it discusses the enforceability of a judge's ruling from another madhhab: a Hanafi judge cannot enforce a non-Hanafi ruling unless it is from a mujtahid judge in a discretionary matter. Finally, it covers the requirement of acceptance (qabul) from the wife. The husband's statement like 'ikhtali'i' is an order for divorce, and if she accepts, she is divorced. If he says 'ishteri nafsaki' it is not a direct order for khul' and requires explicit offer. The passage ends with a reference to the mashayikh not requiring intention for khul' due to common usage.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Judicial determination; what is apparent in court.
ديانة (diyana): Before Allah; the internal truth known only to Allah.
مذاكرة الطلاق (mudhakara al-talaq): Discussion of divorce; considered equivalent to intention (niyya) for kinayat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the husband says 'I divorce you for $1000' and later claims he did not intend divorce, how do the courts treat his claim?
A) The courts accept his claim because divorce requires intention.
B) The courts do not accept his claim because mentioning compensation indicates intention.
C) The courts investigate his true intention before ruling.
D) The courts rule that the marriage continues.

Key Takeaway
Khul' is valid whether or not compensation is mentioned; when compensation is mentioned, the husband's denial of intention is irrelevant in court.

Istithna' (Exception) and the Requirement of Acceptance in Khul'
Explains the rules of istithna' and acceptance in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that a husband's claim of exception (istithna') in khul' is accepted unless the compensation is explicitly mentioned in the contract, and identify when the wife's acceptance is required.

Core Idea
The husband's claim that payment was not for khul' is accepted unless the contract specifies the compensation; acceptance from the wife is required when compensation is mentioned or when using 'ikhtali'i'.

This section delves into the intricacies of the husband's claim of exception (istithna')—that the payment he received was not for the khul' but for another reason. The general rule is that his word is accepted unless the contract explicitly mentions the compensation, which serves as a qarīnah of intent. The passage also clarifies when the wife's acceptance is necessary: when compensation is involved or when the husband uses words like 'khala'tuk' or 'ikhtali'i'. Understanding these conditions ensures that khul' contracts are not misused to circumvent divorce rules.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the general rule of istithna'
The passage from al-Bazzaziyya states: if the husband claims an exception (e.g., that the money he took was a debt, not khul' payment) and the wife denies, his statement is accepted (qawluhu). This is because he is effectively denying the obligation of the khul' payment.
The general rule is that the husband's claim is accepted.
2
Identify the exception to the rule
When the compensation is explicitly mentioned in the khul' contract, the husband's claim of exception is not accepted. The mention of compensation is a qarīnah that the payment was for khul', so his denial is not credible in court.
The exception: if the contract states the compensation, then the claim of exception is invalid.
3
Apply the rule to scenarios
Work through examples: if the husband claims the money was a debt, and the contract did not mention compensation, his claim is accepted. If the contract mentioned compensation, his claim is rejected. But if he claims what he took was a different right (like a deposit), and the contract mentioned compensation, there is a difference of opinion.
The commentator notes ambiguity in Jami' al-Fusulayn.
4
Understand the requirement of acceptance
The passage explains that acceptance (qabul) from the wife is necessary when the khul' is for compensation (i.e., 'iwad) or when the husband uses the word 'khala'tuk' or 'ikhtali'i'. If he uses general kināyah like 'bay' without compensation, acceptance is not required, but intention or discussion of divorce is needed.
Acceptance is not always required; it depends on the wording and presence of compensation.

The exception because he claims upon her the khul' payment and she denies, so the statement is hers. And he has benefited that the occurrence of the bain divorce and its rule will come later in its description: that it is an oath from his side and a contract from her side, so he cannot revoke it, and it is not invalidated by his leaving the session, and it is valid if appended from him, and the rules are reversed regarding her if she starts, as will come. And he did not mention its condition because its condition is the condition of talaq, but acceptance from her is necessary when it is for compensation or with the word khala'tuk or ikhtali'i. Hence in al-Muhit: if he said 'ikhtali'i' and she said 'ikhtala'tu', she is divorced and the mahr falls, because his saying 'ikhtali'i' is an order for talaq with the word khul', and the woman owns talaq by the husband's order, so it becomes like him saying 'tallaqi nafsiki talaqan bā'inan'. Contrary to his saying 'ishtari nafsaki minni' and she said 'ishtaraytu', she is not divorced until the husband says 'bi'tu' because it is an order for khul' which is a contract because the sale is a contract... if the consideration is not mentioned and known, it is not valid. And if he mentions an unknown consideration, such as if he said 'ikhlai' nafsaki bi māl' and she said 'ikhtala'tu nafsi bi alf dirham', the khul' is not complete and she is not divorced until the husband says 'khala'tu' because the delegation of khul' to her is not valid because when he mentioned the consideration, it is in fact a khul', and khul' is not valid without specifying the consideration, and the consideration here is unknown, so it is not valid. And if he mentions a known consideration, such as saying 'ikhlai' nafsaki bi alf dirham' and she says 'ikhtala'tu bi alf dirham', it is a contract... we mentioned and the summary is that his claim of exception is accepted except if he mentioned the consideration in the khul' contract, because the explicit mention of the consideration is an indication of the intention of khul', so he is not believed in his claim to invalidate it by the exception, except if he claims that what he took is not the khul' payment but another right, like a debt or deposit, then his claim of exception is accepted due to the lack of indication... because if his statement is accepted regarding what he took, the khul' with payment does not remain. But there is that the indication of the intention of khul' is the mention of the consideration in the khul', not its receipt afterwards. So if he mentions the consideration, then takes money from her, then claims exception and claims that what he took is another right besides the consideration, the indication of the intention of khul' is not removed, so his claim of exception is not valid and the khul' contract with consideration remains, so his claim that what he took is another right is not accepted because when the consideration remains, the statement is the woman's that what she paid is the khul' payment, not other, because the statement is of the one who conveys (al-mumallik). Thus there is no difference between claiming exception and not, as the statement is the woman's in both cases. What the author mentioned is verbatim in Jami' al-Fusulayn, but he said at its end 'there is consideration' and did not explain its reason. Perhaps what we mentioned is the intention of the author of al-Fusulayn by 'consideration'. And Allah knows best. He said: ('Contrary to if he did not claim the exception') mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya after his saying 'the statement is hers' as text: 'She paid the khul' payment and the husband disputed that he took it in another capacity. Imam Zahir al-Din gave a fatwa that the statement is his, and it is said hers because she is the one who conveyed (al-mumallika).' He said: ('It is dependent on intention or discussion of talaq') Will come at his saying 'and khul' and mubara'a are annulled' that the mashayikh did not require intention in khul' because of the predominance of usage and because it usually occurs after discussion of talaq. So consider.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This lengthy passage covers multiple aspects of khul'. First, the commentator states that the ruling of khul' being bain is general, applying whether or not compensation is mentioned, and with various wordings (khul', bay', mubara'a). However, if compensation is mentioned, the husband's denial of intention for divorce is not accepted in court (qada') but may be true before Allah (diyana). The wife cannot remain with him due to apparent evidence. Then it discusses the rule that discussion of talaq (mudhakara al-talaq) is equivalent to intention for kinayat. Next, it addresses the issue of istithna' (exception): if the husband claims that the compensation he received was not for khul' but for another right, and the wife disputes, his statement is generally accepted (qawluhu) except when the compensation is explicitly mentioned in the contract, which indicates intention for khul'. Then it discusses the enforceability of a judge's ruling from another madhhab: a Hanafi judge cannot enforce a non-Hanafi ruling unless it is from a mujtahid judge in a discretionary matter. Finally, it covers the requirement of acceptance (qabul) from the wife. The husband's statement like 'ikhtali'i' is an order for divorce, and if she accepts, she is divorced. If he says 'ishteri nafsaki' it is not a direct order for khul' and requires explicit offer. The passage ends with a reference to the mashayikh not requiring intention for khul' due to common usage.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): Exception claimed by the husband that the payment was not for khul' but for another reason.
قبول (qabul): Acceptance; the wife's acceptance of the khul' offer.
قرينة (qarīnah): Indication; circumstantial evidence that guides judicial interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When the wife denies the claim.
B) When the contract explicitly mentions the compensation.
C) When the husband did not specify a reason.
D) When the wife has paid the compensation.

Key Takeaway
The husband's claim of exception is accepted unless compensation is explicitly mentioned; acceptance from the wife is required for specific wordings.

Enforceability of Non-Hanafi Judgments: The Dispute over Khul' as Faskh
Discusses enforceability of non-Hanafi rulings on khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on whether a Hanafi judge must enforce a non-Hanafi judge's ruling that khul' is faskh (dissolution) rather than bain divorce.

Core Idea
A mujtahid judge's ruling on khul' as faskh is enforceable by a Hanafi judge, but muqallid judges must only judge by the soundest opinion of their own madhhab.

This passage addresses a critical procedural issue: if a non-Hanafi judge (e.g., a Hanbali) rules that khul' is faskh (judicial dissolution), can a Hanafi judge enforce that ruling? The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq argues that if the judge is a mujtahid, the ruling is enforceable because the matter is open to ijtihad. However, later Hanafi authorities like Shurunbulali and Ibn Abidin hold that muqallid judges cannot enforce opinions contrary to their madhhab. This dispute reflects deeper tensions between ijtihad, taqlid, and judicial authority.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conflicting opinions
The passage presents two views: (1) 'It is said it is enforceable' (qīl yunfadh) and (2) 'It is said it is not' (qīl lā). The first refers to the view that a Hanafi judge may enforce a non-Hanafi ruling on khul' as faskh. The second, supported by Shurunbulali, argues that judges must only use the soundest opinion of their own madhhab.
The key variable is whether the original judge is a mujtahid or a muqallid.
2
Identify the justification for enforceability
The author of al-Bahr argues that if the judge is a mujtahid and his ruling does not contradict a clear text of Quran, well-known sunna, or consensus, it is enforceable. This is because such matters are within the scope of ijtihad.
The ruling on khul' being faskh vs. bain is a discretionary area (mujtahad fīh).
3
Recognize the position of later Hanafi authorities
Shurunbulali and others insist that judges in their time are muqallids and must only follow the relied-upon (mu'tamad) opinion of their madhhab. Ruling by a weak opinion (marjūḥ) or contrary to the madhhab is invalid and the judge may be dismissed.
This is especially stressed in the context of sultanic decrees prohibiting weak opinions.
4
Apply to the khul' case
If a Hanbali judge rules khul' is faskh, and the case is raised to a Hanafi judge, according to the author's view, if the Hanbali judge is a mujtahid, the Hanafi judge enforces it. According to the later view, the Hanafi judge must not enforce it because the mu'tamad in the Hanafi school is that khul' is bain, not faskh.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf) is clear: whether the woman can remarry immediately or must wait for a divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عالم بما في سره لكن لا. المرأة أن تقيم معه لأنها كالقاضي لا تعرف منه إلا الظاهر؛ كذا يسع في المبسوط . وحال مذاكرة الطلاق كالنية كذا في الخانية. وفي البزازية ادعى الاستثناء أو الشرط في الخلع وكذبته فيه فالقول له إلى أن قال: والفتوى على صحة دعوى المغير والمبطل إلا إذا ظهر ما ذكرنا من التزام البدل أو قبضه أو نحوه ادعى الاستثناء وقال قبضت ما قبضت منك بحق لي عليك وقالت بل لبدل الخلع فالقول له لأنه أنكر وجوب البدل عليها وأقر أن له عليها مالاً واحداً لا مالين والمرأة مقرة أن له عليها مالاً آخر فيكون القول له بخلاف ما إذا لم يدع بالطلاق الرجعي فقط لعدم لزوم المال والرجعي يلحق البائن بخلاف ما إذا طلقها بمال ثم خلعها فإنه يلزم المال ولا يصح الخلع لأنها بانت منه بالطلاق قوله : قيل ينفذ وقيل لا) قال في الشرنبلالية : إن قضاة هذا الزمان ليس لهم إلا القضاء بالصحيح من المذهب وهو كونه بائناً اهـ. قال في حاشية مسكين وذكر في ديباجة الدر المختار نقلاً عن الشيخ قاسم في تصحيحه أن الحكم والإفتاء بالقول المرجوح جهل وخرق للإجماع وأن الخلاف خاص بالقاضي المجتهد، وأما المقلد فلا ينفذ قضاؤه بخلاف مذهبه أصلاً كما في القنية، ولا سيما في زماننا فإن السلطان ينص في منشوره على نهيه عن القضاء بالأقوال الضعيفة فكيف بخلاف مذهبه فيكون معزولاً بالنسبة لغير المعتمد من مذهبه فلا ينفذ قضاؤه فيه وينقض كما بسط في قضاء الفتح والبحر والنهر فكان ما في البحر هنا من قوله والظاهر النفاذ خلاف المعتمد .اهـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه فإن مراد المؤلف أنه لو قضى به قاض يرى كونه فسخاً كالحنبلي ينفذ قضاؤه لكونه في فصل مجتهد فيه ليس مما خالف كتاباً ولا سنة مشهورة ولا إجماعا، وإذا رفع لحنفي أمضاه أما لو كان واحداً مما ذكر فإنه ينقضه لعدم نفاذ القضاء فيها كما يأتي بيانه إن شاء الله تعالى في محله قوله: ادعى الاستثناء الخ) هذا كالاستثناء من قوله «إلا إذا ظهر ما الاستثناء لأنه يدعي عليها بدل الخلع وهي تنكر فالقول لها اهـ وأما إذا لم يذكر العوض فهو من الكنايات فيتوقف على النية أو مذاكرة الطلاق إن كان بلفظ الخلع أو المباراة، وإن كان بلفظ البيع كبعت نفسك أو طلاقك فلا لأنه خلاف الظاهر. وقد أفاد بوقوع البائن حكمه وسيأتي بيان صفته أنه يمين من جانبه معاوضة من جانبها فلا يصح رجوعه عنه ولا يبطل بقيامه عن المجلس وصح مضافاً منه وانعكست الأحكام في حقها لو بدأت كما سيأتي. ولم يذكر شرطه لأن شرطه شرط الطلاق ولكن لا بد من القبول منها حيث كان على مال أو كان بلفظ خالعتك أو اختلعي ولذا قال في المحيط : لو قال لها اختلعي فقالت اختلعت تطلق ويسقط المهر لأن قوله «اختلعي أمر بالطلاق بلفظ الخلع والمرأة تملك الطلاق بأمر الزوج فصار بمنزلة ما لو قال لها طلقي نفسك طلاقاً بائناً بخلاف قوله اشتري نفسك مني فقالت اشتريت لا تطلق ما لم يقل الزوج بعت لأنه أمر بالخلع الذي هو معاوضة لأن الشراء معاوضة الأمر إذا لم يكن البدل مذكوراً معلوماً . يصح فلا وأما إذا ذكر مالاً مجهولاً بأن قال اخلعي نفسك بمال فقالت اختلعت نفسي بألف درهم لا يتم الخلع ولا تطلق حتى يقول الزوج خلعت لأنه لم يصح تفويض الخلع إليها لأنه إذا ذكر المال كان خلعاً حقيقة والخلع لا يصح إلا بتسمية البدل والبدل ها هنا مجهول فلم يصح، وإن ذكر مالاً معلوماً بأن قال اخلعي نفسك بألف درهم فقالت اختعلت بألف درهم عقد ذكرنا الخ وحاصله أن دعواه الاستثناء مقبولة إلا إذا ذكر في عقد الخلع البدل فإن التصريح بذكر البدل قرينة على قصد الخلع فلا يصدق في دعوى إبطاله بالاستثناء إلا إذا ادعى أن ما قبضه ليس بدل الخلع بل هو حق آخر كدين أو وديعة فتقبل حينئذ دعواه الاستثناء لانتفاء القرينة لأنه إذا كان القول قوله فيما قبضه لم يبق الخلع ببدل لكن فيه أن القرينة على قصد الخلع هي ذكر البدل في الخلع لا قبضه بعده، فإذا ذكر البدل ثم قبض منها مالاً ثم ادعى الاستثناء وادعى أن ما قبضه حق آخر غير البدل لم تنتف قرينة قصد الخلع فلا تصح دعواه الاستثناء ويبقى عقد الخلع ببدل فلا تقبل دعواه أن ما قبضه حق آخر لأنه حيث بقي البدل يكون القول للمرأة في أن ما دفعته بدل الخلع لا غيره لأن القول للمملكة، وحينئذ فلم يبق فرق بين دعوى الاستثناء وعدمها حيث يكون القول للمرأة في الصورتين، وما ذكره المؤلف مذكور بعينه في جامع الفصولين لكنه قال في آخره وفيه نظر ولم يبين وجهه، ولعل ما ذكرناه هو مراد صاحب الفصولين بالنظر والله سبحانه أعلم قوله : (بخلاف ما إذا لم يدع الاستثناء الخ ذكر في البزازية عقب قوله فالقول لها» ما نصه : دفعت بدل الخلع ورغم الزوج أنه قبضه بجهة أخرى أفتى الإمام ظهير الدين أن القول له وقيل لها لأنها المملكة قوله : (فيتوقف على النية أو مذاكرة الطلاق الخ) سيأتي عند قوله ويسقط الخلع والمباراة الخ» أن المشايخ لم يشترطوا النية في الخلع لغلبة الاستعمال ولأن الغالب كونه بعد مذاكرة الطلاق الخ فتأمل
He made it general, so it includes when it is without compensation also, and when it occurs with the word khul', sale (bay'), or barā'a, and when he did not intend talaq by it but on condition of mentioning the compensation, such that if he said 'I did not intend talaq' along with mentioning it, he is not believed in qada (judicially) but is believed in diyana (before Allah), because Allah knows what is in his secret, but the woman cannot live with him because she, like the judge, only knows the apparent. Thus is it in al-Mabsut. And the state of discussing talaq is like intention (niyya) as in al-Khaniyya. And in al-Bazzaziyya: if he claims an exception (istithnā) or condition (shart) in khul' and she denies him, then the statement is his (qawl lahu) until he says: and the fatwa is on the validity of the claim of the changer and invalidator, except if what we mentioned of the undertaking of the payment or its receipt or similar appears. He claimed an exception and said: I took what I took from you as a right you owed me, and she said: Rather it is for the khul' payment, then the statement is his because he denied the obligation of the payment upon her and affirmed that she owes him one property, not two, and the woman confirms that she owes him another property, so the statement is his, contrary to if he did not claim... For revocable divorce only because no property is binding, and the revocable attaches to the irrevocable, contrary to if he divorced her for property then performed khul' with her, then the property is binding and the khul' is not valid because she has become irrevocably separated from him by the divorce. He said: ('It is said it is enforceable and it is said it is not'). Al-Shurnublaliyya said: The judges of this time have no choice but to judge by the soundest (asahh) of the madhhab, which is that it is bain. Said in Hashiyat Miskin: and mentioned in the introduction of al-Durr al-Mukhtar, quoting from Shaykh Qasim in his correction, that ruling and giving fatwa by the weak opinion (marjuh) is ignorance and violates consensus, and that disagreement is specific to the mujtahid judge; as for the muqallid, his judgment contrary to his madhhab is not enforceable at all, as in al-Quniyya, especially in our time; the ruler stipulates in his decree the prohibition of judging by weak sayings, so how about contrary to his madhhab? So he is dismissed regarding non-reliant parts of his madhhab, so his judgment is not enforceable and is annulled, as expanded in Qada' al-Fath, al-Bahr, and al-Nahr. So what is in al-Bahr here from his saying 'the apparent is enforceability' is contrary to the relied-upon. It is not hidden what is in it, for the intention of the author is that if a judge ruled that it is a dissolution (faskh) like a Hanbali, his judgment is enforceable because it is in a discretionary matter that does not oppose a clear book, a well-known sunna, or consensus. And if it is raised to a Hanafi, he enforces it. But if it is one of what was mentioned, he annuls it due to lack of enforceability, as will come in its place. He said: ('Claimed exception etc.') This is like an exception from his saying 'except if what appeared...' The exception because he claims upon her the khul' payment and she denies, so the statement is hers. And if the payment is not mentioned, it is from the indirect expressions (kinayat), so it is dependent on intention or discussion of talaq if it is with the word khul' or barā'a, and if with the word bay' (sale) like 'I sold you yourself' or 'your talaq', then no, because it contradicts the apparent. And he has benefited that the occurrence of the bain divorce and its rule will come later in its description: that it is an oath from his side and a contract from her side, so he cannot revoke it, and it is not invalidated by his leaving the session, and it is valid if appended from him, and the rules are reversed regarding her if she starts, as will come. And he did not mention its condition because its condition is the condition of talaq, but acceptance from her is necessary when it is for compensation or with the word khala'tuk or ikhtali'i. Hence in al-Muhit: if he said 'ikhtali'i' and she said 'ikhtala'tu', she is divorced and the mahr falls, because his saying 'ikhtali'i' is an order for talaq with the word khul', and the woman owns talaq by the husband's order, so it becomes like him saying 'tallaqi nafsiki talaqan bā'inan'. Contrary to his saying 'ishtari nafsaki minni' and she said 'ishtaraytu', she is not divorced until the husband says 'bi'tu' because it is an order for khul' which is a contract because the sale is a contract... if the consideration is not mentioned and known, it is not valid. And if he mentions an unknown consideration, such as if he said 'ikhlai' nafsaki bi māl' and she said 'ikhtala'tu nafsi bi alf dirham', the khul' is not complete and she is not divorced until the husband says 'khala'tu' because the delegation of khul' to her is not valid because when he mentioned the consideration, it is in fact a khul', and khul' is not valid without specifying the consideration, and the consideration here is unknown, so it is not valid. And if he mentions a known consideration, such as saying 'ikhlai' nafsaki bi alf dirham' and she says 'ikhtala'tu bi alf dirham', it is a contract... we mentioned and the summary is that his claim of exception is accepted except if he mentioned the consideration in the khul' contract, because the explicit mention of the consideration is an indication of the intention of khul', so he is not believed in his claim to invalidate it by the exception, except if he claims that what he took is not the khul' payment but another right, like a debt or deposit, then his claim of exception is accepted due to the lack of indication... because if his statement is accepted regarding what he took, the khul' with payment does not remain. But there is that the indication of the intention of khul' is the mention of the consideration in the khul', not its receipt afterwards. So if he mentions the consideration, then takes money from her, then claims exception and claims that what he took is another right besides the consideration, the indication of the intention of khul' is not removed, so his claim of exception is not valid and the khul' contract with consideration remains, so his claim that what he took is another right is not accepted because when the consideration remains, the statement is the woman's that what she paid is the khul' payment, not other, because the statement is of the one who conveys (al-mumallik). Thus there is no difference between claiming exception and not, as the statement is the woman's in both cases. What the author mentioned is verbatim in Jami' al-Fusulayn, but he said at its end 'there is consideration' and did not explain its reason. Perhaps what we mentioned is the intention of the author of al-Fusulayn by 'consideration'. And Allah knows best. He said: ('Contrary to if he did not claim the exception') mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya after his saying 'the statement is hers' as text: 'She paid the khul' payment and the husband disputed that he took it in another capacity. Imam Zahir al-Din gave a fatwa that the statement is his, and it is said hers because she is the one who conveyed (al-mumallika).' He said: ('It is dependent on intention or discussion of talaq') Will come at his saying 'and khul' and mubara'a are annulled' that the mashayikh did not require intention in khul' because of the predominance of usage and because it usually occurs after discussion of talaq. So consider.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This lengthy passage covers multiple aspects of khul'. First, the commentator states that the ruling of khul' being bain is general, applying whether or not compensation is mentioned, and with various wordings (khul', bay', mubara'a). However, if compensation is mentioned, the husband's denial of intention for divorce is not accepted in court (qada') but may be true before Allah (diyana). The wife cannot remain with him due to apparent evidence. Then it discusses the rule that discussion of talaq (mudhakara al-talaq) is equivalent to intention for kinayat. Next, it addresses the issue of istithna' (exception): if the husband claims that the compensation he received was not for khul' but for another right, and the wife disputes, his statement is generally accepted (qawluhu) except when the compensation is explicitly mentioned in the contract, which indicates intention for khul'. Then it discusses the enforceability of a judge's ruling from another madhhab: a Hanafi judge cannot enforce a non-Hanafi ruling unless it is from a mujtahid judge in a discretionary matter. Finally, it covers the requirement of acceptance (qabul) from the wife. The husband's statement like 'ikhtali'i' is an order for divorce, and if she accepts, she is divorced. If he says 'ishteri nafsaki' it is not a direct order for khul' and requires explicit offer. The passage ends with a reference to the mashayikh not requiring intention for khul' due to common usage.

Key Terms
بائن (bā'in): Irrevocable divorce; the marriage ends immediately and the husband cannot take the wife back except with a new marriage contract.
فسخ (faskh): Judicial annulment; dissolution of marriage by court order.
مجتهد (mujtahid): A scholar qualified to perform ijtihad (independent legal reasoning).
مقلد (muqallid): A layperson or judge who follows a madhhab without performing ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the passage, what should a Hanafi judge do when presented with a Hanbali judge's ruling that khul' is faskh?
A) Enforce the ruling because it was made by a mujtahid.
B) Reject the ruling and apply the Hanafi view that khul' is bain.
C) Send the case back for re-trial in a Hanafi court.
D) Accept the ruling only if the wife agrees.

Key Takeaway
The enforceability of a non-Hanafi ruling on khul' as faskh depends on whether the original judge was a mujtahid; the mufta bihi is that muqallid judges cannot enforce such rulings.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Rulings on Khul' Including Istithna' and Kinayah
Commentary on khul' rulings: istithna' and kinayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on istithna' (exception) in khul' contracts and distinguish the rulings when compensation is mentioned versus when it is not.

Core Idea
In khul', the wife's word is taken regarding payment; explicit mention of compensation blocks the husband's claim of exception.

Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. A common dispute arises when the husband claims the payment he received was not for the khul' but for something else — this is called istithna'. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the evidentiary rules and also explains how khul' functions when no compensation is specified (kinayah). Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly adjudicating khul' cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main issues
The passage addresses (a) the husband's claim that the payment was for something other than khul' (istithna'), and (b) khul' without specifying compensation (kinayah).
2
Analyze the rule on istithna'
When the husband claims exception and the wife denies, whose word is taken? Note the exception: if compensation was explicitly mentioned in the contract, his claim is not accepted.
The general rule is wife's word; the exception is when compensation is mentioned.
3
Understand the reasoning behind the exception
The mention of compensation is a qarina (indication) that the payment was for khul'. Without that qarina, the husband's claim may be accepted if he claims a different right (e.g., debt).
The passage also discusses the nuance that even if the husband claims a different right after mentioning compensation, the qarina remains.
4
Examine kinayah khul'
When no compensation is mentioned, the wording is allusive; its validity depends on intention or prior discussion of divorce. Contrast with explicit sale wording which is not accepted.
Al-Muhit example: 'ikhtali'i' leads to valid divorce and dropped mahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستثناء لأنه يدعي عليها بدل الخلع وهي تنكر فالقول لها اهـ وأما إذا لم يذكر العوض فهو من الكنايات فيتوقف على النية أو مذاكرة الطلاق إن كان بلفظ الخلع أو المباراة، وإن كان بلفظ البيع كبعت نفسك أو طلاقك فلا لأنه خلاف الظاهر. وقد أفاد بوقوع البائن حكمه وسيأتي بيان صفته أنه يمين من جانبه معاوضة من جانبها فلا يصح رجوعه عنه ولا يبطل بقيامه عن المجلس وصح مضافاً منه وانعكست الأحكام في حقها لو بدأت كما سيأتي. ولم يذكر شرطه لأن شرطه شرط الطلاق ولكن لا بد من القبول منها حيث كان على مال أو كان بلفظ خالعتك أو اختلعي ولذا قال في المحيط : لو قال لها اختلعي فقالت اختلعت تطلق ويسقط المهر لأن قوله «اختلعي أمر بالطلاق بلفظ الخلع والمرأة تملك الطلاق بأمر الزوج فصار بمنزلة ما لو قال لها طلقي نفسك طلاقاً بائناً بخلاف قوله اشتري نفسك مني فقالت اشتريت لا تطلق ما لم يقل الزوج بعت لأنه أمر بالخلع الذي هو معاوضة لأن الشراء معاوضة الأمر إذا لم يكن البدل مذكوراً معلوماً . يصح فلا وأما إذا ذكر مالاً مجهولاً بأن قال اخلعي نفسك بمال فقالت اختلعت نفسي بألف درهم لا يتم الخلع ولا تطلق حتى يقول الزوج خلعت لأنه لم يصح تفويض الخلع إليها لأنه إذا ذكر المال كان خلعاً حقيقة والخلع لا يصح إلا بتسمية البدل والبدل ها هنا مجهول فلم يصح، وإن ذكر مالاً معلوماً بأن قال اخلعي نفسك بألف درهم فقالت اختعلت بألف درهم عقد ذكرنا الخ وحاصله أن دعواه الاستثناء مقبولة إلا إذا ذكر في عقد الخلع البدل فإن التصريح بذكر البدل قرينة على قصد الخلع فلا يصدق في دعوى إبطاله بالاستثناء إلا إذا ادعى أن ما قبضه . ليس بدل الخلع بل هو حق آخر كدين أو وديعة فتقبل حينئذ دعواه الاستثناء لانتفاء القزينة لأنه إذا كان القول قوله فيما قبضه لم يبق الخلع ببدل لكن فيه أن القرينة على قصد الخلع هي ذكر البدل في الخلع لا قبضه بعده ، فإذا ذكر البدل ثم قبض منها مالاً ثم ادعى الاستثناء وادعى أن ما قبضه حق آخر غير البدل لم تنتف قرينة قصد الخلع فلا تصح دعواه الاستثناء ويبقى عقد الخلع ببدل فلا تقبل دعواه أن ما قبضه حق آخر لأنه حيث بقي البدل يكون القول للمرأة في أن ما دفعته بدل الخلع لا غيره لأن القول للمملك، وحينئذ فلم يبق فرق بين دعوى الاستثناء وعدمها حيث يكون القول للمرأة في الصورتين، وما ذكره المؤلف مذكور بعينه في جامع الفصولين لكنه قال في آخره وفيه نظر ولم يبين وجهه، ولعل ما ذكرناه هو مراد صاحب الفصولين بالنظر والله سبحانه أعلم قوله : (بخلاف ما إذا لم يدع الاستثناء الخ ذكر في البزازية عقب قوله فالقول لها» ما نصه : دفعت بدل الخلع ورغم الزوج أنه قبضه بجهة أخرى أفتى الإمام ظهير الدين أن القول له وقيل لها لأنها المملكة قوله : (فيتوقف على النية أو مذاكرة الطلاق الخ) سيأتي عند قوله ويسقط الخلع والمباراة الخ» أن المشايخ لم يشترطوا النية في الخلع لغلبة الاستعمال ولأن الغالب كونه بعد مذاكرة الطلاق الخ فتأمل
The exception: because he claims the compensation for khul' from her and she denies, so the statement is hers. As for when the compensation is not mentioned, it is from kinayah (allusive speech) and depends on intention or discussion of divorce. If it is with the wording 'khul'' or 'mubara'ah', then it is kinayah; if with the wording of sale like 'I sold you' or 'your divorce', then it is not, because it is contrary to the apparent. And it benefits with the occurrence of ba'in (irrevocable) its ruling. The description will come that it is an oath from his side and a transaction from her side. So his withdrawal from it is not valid, and it is not invalidated by his standing up from the session, and it is valid as muḍāf (deferred) from him. The rulings are reversed in her favor if she started. And he did not mention its condition because its condition is the condition of divorce, but acceptance from her is necessary when it is in exchange for wealth or with the wording 'I gave you khul'' or 'divorce yourself'. For this reason, al-Muhit said: If he says 'divorce yourself' and she says 'I divorced myself', she is divorced and the mahr is dropped because his saying 'divorce yourself' is an order for divorce with the wording of khul', and the woman owns the divorce by the husband's order. So it becomes like his saying 'divorce yourself with a ba'in divorce'. Contrary to his saying 'buy yourself from me' and she says 'I bought', she is not divorced until the husband says 'I sold' because it is an order for khul' which is a transaction. Purchase is a transaction when the compensation is not mentioned and known. As for when he mentions unknown wealth, like he says 'divorce yourself with wealth' and she says 'I divorced myself with a thousand dirhams', the khul' is not complete and she is not divorced until the husband says 'I divorced her' because delegation of khul' to her is not valid. When he mentions wealth, it is khul' literally, and khul' is not valid without specifying the compensation, and the compensation here is unknown, so it is not valid. And if he mentions known wealth, like he says 'divorce yourself with a thousand dirhams' and she says 'I divorced myself with a thousand dirhams', we have mentioned the contract. The summary is that his claim of exception is accepted except when he mentions the compensation in the khul' contract. Mentioning the compensation is an indication of his intent for khul', so he is not believed in his claim to invalidate it by exception unless he claims that what he took is not the compensation for khul' but another right like a debt or trust, then his claim of exception is accepted because the indication is absent. Because if his word is taken regarding what he took, the khul' with compensation remains. But there is a point: the indication of intent for khul' is the mention of the compensation in the khul', not its receipt afterwards. So if he mentioned the compensation then took money from her, then claimed exception and claimed that what he took is another right besides the compensation, the indication of intent for khul' is not removed, so his claim of exception is not valid, and the khul' contract with compensation remains. So his claim that what he took is another right is not accepted because where the compensation remains, the statement is the woman's that what she paid is the compensation for khul', not other, because the statement is of the one who pays. So there is no difference between claiming exception and not claiming it, as the woman's statement holds in both cases. What the author mentioned is found in Jami' al-Fusulayn, but he said at the end 'and there is consideration' and did not clarify his reason. Perhaps what we mentioned is the intent of the author of al-Fusulayn by 'consideration', and Allah knows best. His statement: (contrary to when he does not claim exception...) mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya after his statement 'the statement is hers', text: 'She paid the compensation for khul' and the husband claimed that he took it for another reason; Imam Zahir al-Din gave a fatwa that his statement holds, and it was said hers because she is the payer.' His statement: (it depends on intention or discussion of divorce...) will come at his statement 'and khul' and mubara'ah are dropped' that the mashayikh did not require intention in khul' due to common usage and because it is usually after discussion of divorce. So reflect.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of khul' from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering two main issues: the ruling on the husband's claim of exception (istithna') regarding the compensation, and the ruling when no compensation is mentioned (kinayah). The author begins by stating that if the husband claims the compensation was not for khul' but for something else, and the wife denies, the wife's word is taken because she is the one who paid. However, if the compensation was explicitly mentioned in the khul' contract, that mention is a strong indication that the payment was indeed for khul', so the husband's claim of exception is not accepted unless he can show the payment was for another right like a debt. The author then discusses kinayah: if no compensation is mentioned, the khul' is considered allusive and depends on intention or if the couple had been discussing divorce. Specific wordings like 'khul'' or 'mubara'ah' are kinayah, while sale wordings like 'I sold you' are not. The author also notes that khul' with known compensation requires the wife's acceptance; examples from al-Muhit illustrate that if the husband says 'ikhtali'i' (divorce yourself) and she says 'ikhtala'tu', she is divorced and the mahr drops, but if he says 'ishtari nafsaki' (buy yourself), she is not divorced until he says 'bi'tu' (I sold). When the compensation is unknown, the khul' is invalid until the husband specifies. The passage concludes with a note that later scholars did not require intention in khul' due to common usage.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithnā'): The husband's claim that the payment he received from his wife is not the compensation for khul' but something else (e.g., a debt).
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce by redemption where the wife pays compensation to the husband in exchange for her release.
الكناية (al-kināyah): Allusive speech that requires intention or context to determine the meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife, 'Ikhtali'i' (divorce yourself) without mentioning compensation, and she says 'Ikhtala'tu', what is the ruling according to Al-Muhit?
A) She is not divorced until he specifies compensation.
B) She is divorced and the mahr is dropped.
C) She is divorced but must pay a compensation.
D) The khul' is invalid because compensation is required.

Key Takeaway
The wife's word is taken regarding payment in khul' unless compensation was explicitly mentioned, in which case the husband cannot claim otherwise.

Acceptance in Khul' and Conditional Khul'
Rulings on acceptance, conditional khul', and specific phrasings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid acceptance in khul', distinguish between suspended (mu'allaq) and deferred (muḍāf) khul', and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the husband's need to say 'bi'tu'.

Core Idea
Khul' with compensation is a transaction; the husband's explicit acceptance is required, and acceptance before a condition or time is generally invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the nuances of acceptance in khul', especially when compensation is involved. The author, Ibn Nujaym, navigates internal Hanafi disputes and harmonizes conflicting narrations. You will learn the precise conditions for acceptance, the timing issues in suspended and deferred khul', and the critical role of the husband's wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The passage first addresses a dispute: when khul' is with known compensation, is it completed by the wife's acceptance alone or does it require the husband's explicit 'bi'tu' (I sold)? Note that there are two narrations within the Hanafi school.
This dispute also applies to kitabah (manumission contract) and sulh for intentional homicide.
2
Analyze the reasoning
The author explains from al-Nawadir that the correct view (sahih) requires the husband's 'bi'tu' because khul' with compensation is a transaction (mu'awada) akin to sale, which requires mutual offer and acceptance. Without the husband's explicit acceptance, the transaction is incomplete unless he intended confirmation (tahqiq) rather than bargaining.
The phrase 'الخلع معاوضة يتم بركن واحد' indicates that some consider it completed by one party's action, but the sahih view insists on mutual consent.
3
Explore timing: suspended (mu'allaq) vs deferred (muḍāf)
The passage discusses when acceptance must occur. In suspended khul' (conditional), acceptance is generally only valid after the condition occurs. In deferred khul' (time-based), acceptance is valid only after the time arrives. However, al-Tajnis reports a narration allowing acceptance before the condition if parties mutually agree. The author suggests a harmonization: acceptance before time in deferred is valid because the offer is a cause (sabab) for the present, while in suspended it is not.
This distinction is based on usul principles: the suspended offer is nonexistent before the condition, so acceptance is impossible.
4
Apply to specific phrasings
The passage then provides rulings on various phrases: her saying 'fa'altu' is not acceptance unless intended as confirmation; the husband's answer 'anti taliq' to her request 'ikhla'ni' is equivalent to 'khala'tuki'; selling divorce for mahr requires her knowing acceptance; and if he says 'bi'tu minki talaqaki bi-mahriki' and she says 'tallaqtu nafsi', it is valid and she owes the mahr.
These detailed scenarios illustrate how the principles apply in practice.
