Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on khul', focusing on the requirement of acceptance in different scenarios and conditional khul'. The author discusses a dispute over whether khul' with known compensation is completed if the husband does not explicitly say 'khala'tu' (I gave khul') and the wife says 'ikhtala'tu' (I divorced myself) without the husband's explicit acceptance. In one narration it is complete, in another it is not. This dispute also applies to kitabah (contract of manumission) and sulh (settlement) for intentional homicide. The author then quotes from al-Nawadir that if the husband says 'ishtarayti minni thalatha talaqat' (you bought from me three divorces) and she says 'ishtaraytu' (I bought), the khul' is not complete until he says 'bi'tu' (I sold), and this is the correct view unless he intended confirmation (tahqiq) rather than bargaining. Next, the author presents a ruling from Jami' al-Fusulayn that every divorce that occurs with a condition that is not wealth is raj'i (revocable). The discussion then moves to acceptance in suspended (mu'allaq) and deferred (muḍāf) khul'. According to al-Kafi, acceptance in a deferred khul' is valid only after the time arrives, while in a suspended khul', acceptance is valid only after the condition occurs. However, al-Tajnis reports a narration that acceptance can be valid before the condition if the parties mutually agree. The author suggests a harmonization: acceptance before time in deferred khul' is valid because it is a cause, while in suspended it is not, because it is not a cause. Further rulings from al-Mujtaba: if the husband sells the divorce for the mahr, she is discharged from the mahr and the divorce is raj'i. The wife must know the meaning of her acceptance. If she is prompted to say 'ikhtala'tu' without understanding, it is not valid because khul' is a transaction, unlike divorce, manumission, and tadbir (pure relinquishment). The passage also covers that her saying 'fa'altu' (I did) in response is not an acceptance unless intended as confirmation. If the wife says 'ikhla'ni' and the husband responds 'anti taliq', it is like his saying 'khala'tuki'. If the husband says 'bi'tu minki talaqaki bi-mahriki' and she says 'tallaqtu nafsi', she becomes divorced and must pay the mahr. The author concludes with notes from al-Tatarakhaniyya and al-Ramli emphasizing that the divorce in such cases remains raj'i despite being counterbalanced by wealth.

Key Terms
القبول (al-qabūl): Acceptance; in khul', the wife's acceptance of the husband's offer is required when compensation is involved.
المعلق (al-mu'allaq): Suspended (conditional) divorce, where the divorce is contingent on a future event.
المضاف (al-muḍāf): Deferred divorce, where the divorce is assigned to a future time.

In khul' with compensation, the husband's explicit acceptance (bi'tu) is required when using sale wording, and acceptance must generally occur after the condition or time in suspended/deferred khul'.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Is Khul' Completed Without Explicit Acceptance?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khul' acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi narrations on the completion of khul' and apply the preferred view (mufta bihi) to scenarios where the wife initiates without explicit acceptance.

Core Idea
Khul' is an exchange; without the husband's explicit 'I sold', it is not completed unless he intended confirmation.

The Hanafi school contains a nuanced internal dispute regarding the completion of khul' when the wife does not explicitly say 'I accept'. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq examines two narrations and clarifies the preferred view, emphasizing that khul' is a contract of exchange requiring proper offer and acceptance. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between different transmissions within the madhhab and apply the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
Recognize that the disagreement is about whether khul' is completed when the wife initiates (e.g., says 'Divorce me for a thousand') and the husband responds without saying 'I sold' (bā‘tu).
The dispute is intra-Hanafi, not with another school.
2
State the Two Narrations
One narration holds that khul' is completed (implicit acceptance suffices); the other holds it is not completed unless the husband explicitly says 'I sold'.
The same two narrations apply to kitāba (contract of manumission) and ṣulḥ for intentional bloodshed.
3
Examine the Preferred View (al-Nawādir)
According to al-Nawādir, the correct view is that khul' is not completed unless the husband says 'I sold', unless he intended confirmation (taḥqīq) rather than negotiation (musāwamah).
The rationale: khul' is a mu‘āwaḍah (exchange), and a command to perform khul' is not an offer.
4
Apply to Analogous Cases
The same rule applies if the wife says 'I bought three divorces' – the husband's 'I sold' is required. Note the contrast with marriage (nikāḥ), where the wife's 'I bought' is not analogized because nikāḥ is not a pure exchange.
This highlights the Hanafi characterization of khul' as a sale-like contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خالعت ولم يقل الزوج خلعت أو قالت المرأة خالعني بألف فقال الزوج ولم تقل المرأة قبلت تم الخلع في رواية ولم يتم في أخرى والكتابة والصلح عن دم العمد على الروايتين . وكذا لو قال اشترى ثلاث تطليقات بكذا فقالت اشتريت بخلاف النكاح. وفي النوادر : لو قال لها اشتريت مني ثلاث تطليقات بكذا فقالت اشتريت لا يتم الخلع ما لم يقل الزوج بعت وهو الصحيح إلا إذا أراد به التحقيق دون المساومة لأنه لم يوجد الأمر بالخلع والخلع معاوضة يتم بركن واحد اهـ.
She performed khul' and the husband did not say 'I have divorced [by khul']', or the woman said 'Divorce me [by khul'] for one thousand' and the husband said [something] and the woman did not say 'I accept', the khul' is completed in one narration and not completed in another. And the [rules of] kitābah and sulh for intentional bloodshed follow the two narrations. Similarly, if he said 'Buy three divorces for such-and-such' and she said 'I bought', unlike marriage. And in al-Nawādir: If he said to her 'Buy from me three divorces for such-and-such' and she said 'I bought', the khul' is not completed unless the husband says 'I sold', and that is the correct [view], unless he intended confirmation, not negotiation, because the command for khul' did not occur, and khul' is an exchange that is completed with one pillar.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq discusses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the completion of khul' when the wife does not explicitly say 'I accept'. There are two narrations: one says the khul' is completed (based on the idea that the wife's action of initiating implies acceptance), the other says it is not completed because khul' is a contract of exchange requiring explicit offer and acceptance. The same dispute applies to kitāba (contract of manumission) and sulh for intentional homicide. The author then cites al-Nawādir, where the correct view is that the husband must say 'I sold' (bā‘tu) for the khul' to be valid, unless he intended confirmation (taḥqīq) rather than negotiation (musāwamah). The rationale is that khul' is a mu‘āwaḍah (exchange) and is completed with only one pillar (rukn), but the offer and acceptance are still required.

Key Terms
خلع (khul‘): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid by her to the husband.
مُعاوضة (mu‘āwaḍah): A contract of exchange where consideration is given for a benefit.
رواية (riwāyah): A narration or transmission of a legal ruling from the early Hanafi imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the preferred view on khul' requires the husband's explicit 'I sold' for acceptance, unless he intended confirmation, underscoring the exchange nature of khul'.

When Acceptance is Valid in Conditional and Time-Based Khul'
Rulings on when acceptance is valid in khul' that is conditional or tied to a future time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mu'allaq and mudaf khul' regarding the timing of acceptance and apply the Hanafi reconciliation based on the presence of the cause.

Core Idea
Acceptance in time-based khul' can be valid before the time because the cause exists; in conditional khul' it is not until the condition occurs.

This lesson addresses a classical Hanafi disagreement about when a wife may accept an offer of khul' that is either suspended on a condition (mu'allaq) or tied to a future time (mudaf). The author reconciles conflicting narrations by considering whether the underlying cause (sabab) is present at the moment of acceptance, a subtle application of qiyas khafi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of khul'
Recognize that mu'allaq is suspended on a condition (e.g., 'if you enter the house'), while mudaf is tied to a future time (e.g., 'tomorrow').
Mu'allaq: condition. Mudaf: time.
2
State the ruling from al-Kāfī and Jāmi‘ al-Fuṣūlayn
According to these sources, acceptance is only valid after the condition occurs (mu'allaq) or after the time arrives (mudaf), because the offer is non-existent before that.
3
Note the contradicting narration from al-Tajnīs
Al-Tajnīs reports a case where mutual agreement before the condition made khul' valid, suggesting early acceptance is possible.
This creates an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyse the author's reconciliation
The author proposes: in mudaf, acceptance before the time is valid because the marriage (the cause) already exists; in mu'allaq, it is not valid because the cause is absent until the condition is fulfilled.
This distinction is based on the presence of the sabab.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author's view is preferred (mukhtār) as it reconciles the texts. Thus, early acceptance is valid in mudaf but not in mu'allaq.
Earlier sources differ, but later Hanafi fatwa leans toward this distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جامع الفصولين كل طلاق وقع بشرط ليس بمال فهو رجعي، وفيه أن القبول في المعلق إنما يكون بعد وجود الشرط. وفي الكافي : القبول في المضاف إنما يكون بعد وجود الوقت ولا يصح القبول قبله لأن الإيجاب معلق بالشرط والمعلق بالشرط عدم قبل الشرط فلا يصح القبول قبل الإيجاب .اهـ. وفي التجنيس ما يفيد صحة القبول في المعلق قبل وجود الشرط فإنه قال : لو قال إن دخلت الدار فقد خلعتك على ألف فتراضيا عليه ففعلت صح الخلع. وفي الوجيز كما في الكافي وأقول: لو قيل بصحة القبول في المضاف قبل وجود الوقت لانعقاده سبباً للحال عندنا وبعدم صحته في المعلق قبل وجود الشرط لعدم انعقاده سبباً للحال لكان حسناً لتخريجه على الأصول.
And in Jāmi‘ al-Fuṣūlayn: Every divorce that occurs with a condition not involving wealth is raj‘ī. And in it: Acceptance in a suspended [divorce] only occurs after the existence of the condition. And in al-Kāfī: Acceptance in an added [divorce] only occurs after the existence of the time, and acceptance before it is invalid because the offer is suspended by the condition, and what is suspended by the condition is non-existent before the condition, so acceptance before the offer is not valid. End quote. And in al-Tajnīs: [There is] what indicates the validity of acceptance in the suspended [divorce] before the existence of the condition, for he said: If he said, 'If you enter the house, then I have divorced you [by khul‘] for one thousand,' and they agreed mutually upon it, and she did [enter], the khul‘ is valid. And in al-Wajīz: It is like in al-Kāfī. And I say: If it were said that acceptance in the added [divorce] is valid before the existence of the time because it is concluded as a cause for the present in our view, and that it is not valid in the suspended before the existence of the condition because it is not concluded as a cause for the present, that would be good, based on derivation from principles.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage discusses the timing of acceptance in khul' that is either suspended (mu‘allaq) on a condition or added (muḍāf) to a future time. The author cites Jāmi‘ al-Fuṣūlayn, which states that any divorce occurring with a condition not involving wealth is raj‘ī. In such cases, acceptance (of the khul' offer by the wife) only takes effect after the condition occurs. Al-Kāfī extends this to muḍāf: acceptance is only valid after the time arrives, because the offer is suspended and non-existent before the condition. However, al-Tajnīs reports a contrary narration: if the husband says 'If you enter the house, then I have divorced you [by khul‘] for one thousand' and they mutually agree, and she enters, the khul‘ is valid—implying that acceptance before the condition is valid. The author (in al-Bahr al-Rā’iq) offers a reconciliation: acceptance in muḍāf should be valid before the time because the marriage itself (the cause) is present in our view, whereas in mu‘allaq it should not be valid because the cause is not present until the condition is fulfilled. This is consistent with the principles (uṣūl).

Key Terms
معلق (mu‘allaq): A khul' that is suspended upon the occurrence of a future condition.
مضاف (muḍāf): A khul' that is added to a specific future time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Rā’iq, what distinguishes mudaf from mu'allaq regarding early acceptance?
A) The presence of a condition
B) The presence of the cause (sabab) at the time of acceptance
C) The amount of the khul' payment
D) The intention of the parties

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of acceptance in a conditional or time-based khul' depends on whether the underlying cause (the marital bond) is present at the time of acceptance.

The Condition of Knowledge in Khul' and Offer-Acceptance Scenarios
Rulings on the condition of wife's knowledge in khul' acceptance and various forms of offer and response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the wife's understanding is required in khul', distinguish between mu'awada and iskat, and determine the validity of various offer-acceptance formulations in khul'.

Core Idea
Khul' is a mu'awada (exchange) requiring knowing consent; pure divorce is iskat (annulment) valid even without understanding.

Khul' is a unique form of divorce involving financial compensation. The Hanafi school treats it as an exchange similar to a sale, which carries important legal consequences. One such consequence is the requirement that the wife understand the meaning of her acceptance—a condition not found in pure divorce. This lesson examines several scenarios from classical Hanafi texts that illustrate how the nature of khul' as an exchange shapes its validity conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of khul'
Recognize that khul' is classified as a mu'awada (exchange) because it involves the wife paying compensation in return for divorce. This classification is the key to understanding the rules that apply.
Contrast with talāq (pure divorce), which is an iskāt (annulment) and does not require the wife's consent or understanding.
2
Locate the condition of knowledge
The passage explicitly states that the wife must know the meaning of her acceptance. Identify the source of this condition and the reasoning behind it.
The condition is derived from the analogy (qiyās) to sale, where both parties must understand the transaction.
3
Examine the evidence
The proof is qiyās jaliy: the ‘illa (effective cause) is that khul' is an exchange. Since sale requires knowing consent, so does khul'.
This is different from iskāt, which is valid even with ignorance.
4
Apply to various scenarios
The text presents several scenarios involving different wordings (e.g., 'fa'altu', 'anti tāliq' in response to 'ikhl'anī', conditional khul'). Work through each to see how the condition of knowledge applies or how the nature of khul' affects the ruling.
Pay attention to which scenarios are considered valid and whether the divorce is raj‘ī or bā’in.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf
There are differences of opinion on whether the divorce in some scenarios is raj‘ī or bā’in. Identify the preferred view (mukhtār) and the authority behind it.
The author cites al-Khāniyyah and al-Mujtabā as authoritative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المجتبى : باع طلاقها منها بمهرها فهو براءة من المهر والطلاق رجعي ويشترط في قبولها علمها بمعناه، فلو قال لها اختلعي نفسك بكذا ثم لقنها بالعربية حتى قالت اختلعت وهي لا تعلم بذلك فالصحيح أنه لا يصح ما لم تعلم المرأة ذلك لأنه معاوضة كالبيع بخلاف الطلاق والعتاق والتدبير لأنه إسقاط محض والإسقاط يصح مع الجهل ؛ كذا في المحيط. وقولها فعلت في جواب قوله خلعت نفسك مني بكذا ليس بقبول على الصحيح المختار إلا إذا أراد به التحقيق. ولو قالت لزوجها اخلعني على ألف درهم فقال الزوج مجيباً لها أنت طالق صار كقوله خلعتك لأن هذا يحتمل أن يكون جواباً فيجعل جواباً لها وهو المختار كما في الخانية. ولو قال بعت منك طلاقك بمهرك فقالت طلقت نفسي بانت منه بمهرها بمنزلة قولها اشتریت لأنه يصح جواباً ويصح ابتداء فيجعل جواباً لها، وقيل يقع رجعياً والأول أصح. ولو قال لها اخلعي نفسك فقالت قد طلقت لزمها المال إلا أن ينوي بغير مال. ولو قال بعت منك تطليقة فقالت اشتريت يقع الطلاق رجعياً مجاناً لأنه ولو قال لها بعت نفسك صريح . قوله : (كل طلاق وقع بشرط الخ) في التتارخانية عن الخانية : رجل قال لامرأته إذا دخلت الدار فقد خلعتك على ألف فدخلت الدار يقع الطلاق بألف يريد به إذا قبلت عند الدخول اهـ. قوله : (وفي القنية في الباب المعقود إلى قوله (آخرها أي آخر القنية وهو مذكور آخر الأبواب كلها. هذا وقد نقل الرملي عنها زيادة على ما ذكره المؤلف هنا برمز اسنع دبس أن الواقع فيها . رجعي الزوج لاتفاقهما على الرجعي ومقابلته بالمال لا تغيره إلى أن قال: ثم أجاب عن مسألة الزيادات
And in al-Mujtabā: He sold her divorce for her dower, so it is a discharge from the dower and the divorce is raj‘ī. And it is a condition in her acceptance that she knows its meaning. So if he said to her 'Divorce yourself [by khul‘] for such-and-such' and then taught her in Arabic until she said 'I divorced myself' while she does not know that [meaning], the correct [view] is that it is not valid unless the woman knows that, because it is an exchange like a sale, unlike divorce, manumission, and tadbīr because they are mere annulments and annulment is valid with ignorance. Thus in al-Muḥīṭ. And her saying 'I did' in response to his saying 'Divorce yourself from me for such-and-such' is not an acceptance according to the correct and chosen [view] unless he intended confirmation. And if she said to her husband 'Divorce me [by khul‘] for one thousand dirhams' and the husband replied to her 'You are divorced', it becomes like his saying 'I have divorced you [by khul‘]' because this can be a response, so it is made a response to her, and that is the chosen [view] as in al-Khāniyyah. And if he said 'I sold your divorce to you for your dower' and she said 'I divorced myself', she becomes separated from him for her dower, similar to her saying 'I bought' because it is valid as a response and valid as an initiation, so it is made a response to her. And it was said it occurs as raj‘ī, and the first is more correct. And if he said to her 'Divorce yourself' and she said 'I have divorced', the money is incumbent on her unless he intends without property. And if he said 'I sold you a divorce' and she said 'I bought', the divorce occurs as raj‘ī free of charge because... And if he said to her 'I sold you' [it is] explicit. His statement: (Every divorce that occurs with a condition...) in al-Tatārkhāniyyah from al-Khāniyyah: A man said to his wife 'If you enter the house, then I have divorced you [by khul‘] for one thousand,' and she entered the house, the divorce occurs for one thousand, meaning when she accepts at the time of entry. End quote. His statement: (And in al-Qunyah, in the chapter devoted to...) up to his saying (the end of it, i.e., the end of al-Qunyah, and it is mentioned at the end of all chapters.) This, and al-Ramlī has narrated from it an addition to what the author mentioned here with the symbol 'asn‘ dbs' that what occurs in it is raj‘ī... for the husband because of their agreement on the raj‘ī and the exchange for property does not change it, until he said: Then he answered about the issue of al-Ziyādāt.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage covers several important rulings on khul'. First, from al-Mujtabā: when the husband 'sells' the divorce for the dower, it is a discharge from the dower and the divorce is raj‘ī (reversible). The wife must understand the meaning of her acceptance; if the husband teaches her Arabic words and she repeats them without understanding, the khul‘ is invalid. This is because khul‘ is an exchange (like a sale), requiring consent; whereas pure divorce (talāq) and manumission are mere annulments (iskāt) and are valid even if the person does not understand. Second, the phrase 'fa‘altu' (I did) in response to 'khal‘ati nafsaki' is not a valid acceptance unless the husband intended confirmation (taḥqīq). Third, if the wife says 'ikhl‘anī' (divorce me by khul‘) and the husband responds 'anti tāliq' (you are divorced), it is treated as if he said 'khal‘atuki' (I divorce you by khul‘) because the response can be interpreted accordingly. Fourth, various scenarios of offer and acceptance are discussed, with the general principle that the wording must clearly indicate an exchange. The passage also cites al-Tatārkhāniyyah on conditional khul‘, and al-Ramlī's addition from al-Qunyah regarding the nature of the divorce when both parties agree it is raj‘ī.

Key Terms
إسقاط (iskāt): A pure annulment or relinquishment of rights, e.g., talāq or itq.
بائع (bā’i‘): Seller; used metaphorically for the husband in khul‘ as he 'sells' the divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because it is an exchange like a sale
C) Because the Quran explicitly requires it
D) Because the husband's consent is not needed

Key Takeaway
Khul' is a financial exchange requiring knowing consent; the wife must understand her acceptance for it to be valid.

Does Money Change a Raj'ī Divorce to Ba’in in Khul‘?
Rulings on khul' involving future divorces and the effect of monetary exchange on divorce type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a khul‘ divorce with money changes from raj‘ī to ba’in and explain the reasoning based on the compensatory nature of the exchange.

Core Idea
In khul‘, money can change a raj‘ī divorce into a ba’in divorce when the wife demands ba’in for compensation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq delves into complex khul‘ scenarios where future divorces and monetary exchanges are involved. The key question is whether the exchange of money alters the legal nature of a raj‘ī divorce. The Hanafi school resolves this by examining the parties' intent and the compensatory function of the bā’ preposition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Is the divorce raj‘ī or ba’in when money is exchanged? The passage presents scenarios where the wife gives up her dower or pays money in exchange for a divorce described as raj‘ī.
The dispute is internal to the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the al-Qunyah scenario
Wife says 'I acquit you of the dower on condition of raj‘ī divorce'; husband pronounces a raj‘ī divorce. The ruling says it becomes ba’in due to the exchange.
3
Understand the reasoning
The bā’ preposition in compensation (e.g., 'for one thousand') necessitates termination of the marriage. If money is given for a divorce, the marriage ends irrevocably.
This reasoning overrides the parties' description.
4
Contrast with mutual agreement
If both parties agree it is raj‘ī and the money is an acquittal without demanding ba’in, it remains raj‘ī and the husband is released from the debt.
The key is the wife's demand.
5
Apply to future divorce cases
Passage shows how the money is apportioned when two divorces are pronounced (one immediate, one future) and how the description is affected.
The principle remains: compensation determines the type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

القبول بعده. ولو قالت المرأة بعت منك مهري ونفقة عدتي فقال اشتريت فالظاهر أنها لا تطلق لأن الزوج ما باع نفسها ولا طلاقها منها إنما اشترى مهرها وهذا لا يكون طلاقاً لكن الأحوط أن يجدد النكاح ؛ كذا في المحيط . وفي القنية في الباب المعقود للمسائل التي لم يوجد فيها رواية ولا جواب شاف للمتأخرين آخرها قالت لزوجها أبرأتك من المهر بشرط الطلاق الرجعي فقال لها أنت طالق طلاقاً رجعياً يقع بائناً للمقابلة في بألف درهم فقبلت وقعت واحدة في الحال بنصف الألف وأخرى غداً بغير شيء، وإن تزوجها قبل مجيء الغد ثم جاء الغد تقع أخرى بخمسمائة . أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة وغداً أخرى بألف فقبلت وقعت واحدة للحال بغير شيء وفي الغد أخرى بالألف، ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم بائنة وغداً أخرى بألف وقع للحال واحدة بائنة بغير شيء وغدا أخرى بالألف. ولو قال أنت فراجعه اهـ . قلت : قد راجعت النسخة التي عندي فلم أر فيها زيادة على ما ذكره المؤلف هنا عنها، وكذا راجعت غير ذلك الباب من مظان المسألة فلم أجد ذلك فلعل نسخته فيها تلك الزيادة والله تعالى أعلم . ثم رأيت ذلك في آخر الحاوي لصاحب القنية حيث قال اسنع دبس : والواقع فيها بالرجعية ولم يتفقا عليها وعند اتفاقهما ورضاهما بالرجعية وتوصيفه بها الطريق الأولى أن الواقع فيه رجعي، ولما كان الواقع به رجعياً فمن ضرورته الإبراء وأما مسألة الزيادات فهي فيما إذا كانت المرأة طالبة (فالألف مقابل بهما مخالف للمسألة الآتية قريباً
From you, and she said 'I bought', the divorce occurs as ba’in because this is a metaphor and it is ba’in. And if he said to her 'I sold you your affair for one thousand dirhams if you choose yourself in the session', the divorce occurs and the money is incumbent on her because he made her the owner of the divorce with money, so if she chooses, she has become owner. And if he said to his wife 'Every woman I marry, I have sold her divorce to you for one dirham' and then he married a woman, the acceptance is hers after the marriage. If she accepts after the marriage, her divorce or his divorce [of her] occurs, but if she accepts before it, it does not occur because this statement of the husband is a khul‘ after marriage, so acceptance after it is required. And if the woman said 'I sold you my dower and my ‘iddah maintenance' and he said 'I bought', apparently she is not divorced because the husband did not sell her nor her divorce from her; he only bought her dower, and this does not constitute divorce, but it is precautionary to renew the marriage. And is the husband released [from the debt] because the condition exists in form or not? End quote. And in al-Dhakhīrah: 'You are divorced one now and tomorrow another for one thousand dirhams' and she accepted, one occurs now for half a thousand and another tomorrow for nothing. And if he marries her before the coming of tomorrow, then tomorrow comes, another occurs for five hundred. 'You are divorced one now, I retain the right of return, and tomorrow another for one thousand' and she accepted, one occurs now for nothing and tomorrow another for one thousand. And if he said 'You are divorced today ba’in and tomorrow another for one thousand', one ba’in occurs now for nothing and tomorrow another for one thousand. And if he said 'You...' review it. I said: I have reviewed the copy I have and did not find any addition to what the author mentioned here from it, and similarly I reviewed other chapters of the subject and did not find that, so perhaps his copy had that addition, and Allah knows best. Then I saw that at the end of al-Ḥāwī by the author of al-Qunyah where he said 'asn‘ dbs': And what occurs in it is raj‘ī, and the husband is released because of their agreement and mutual consent on the occurrence of raj‘ī divorce and its exchange for property after it had been described as raj‘ī, not otherwise. And he mentioned the source for emphasis, as if he said 'You are divorced one divorce', so what occurs is raj‘ī even if he did not describe it as raj‘ī and they did not agree on it. And when they agree and are pleased with the raj‘ī and its description, it is more appropriate that what occurs is raj‘ī. And since what occurs is raj‘ī, release is necessary. As for the issue of al-Ziyādāt, it is when the woman demands from him two ba’in divorces for one thousand, then the exchange for money changes what the husband described as raj‘ī to what she demanded as ba’in because she did not consent to the obligation of the thousand while the marriage persists. So what he described is nullified by the exchange. And because the bā’ (the preposition) accompanies compensations, and the compensation necessitates the compensated, and if it occurs as raj‘ī, the meaning of bā’ would be nullified due to the nullity of the compensated, which is not permissible because the existence of the compensation (obligation of the thousand) necessitates the existence of the compensated (termination of the marriage between them). So what the husband described is nullified by the exchange of the property, and thus both [divorces] occur as ba’in. End quote. His statement: (The one thousand is in exchange for both) contradicts the issue that follows shortly.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage deals with complex scenarios in khul' involving multiple divorces and future divorces. Key points: (1) In some wordings, the divorce occurs as ba’in (irreversible). (2) If the husband says 'I sold your affair for a thousand' and the wife chooses, the divorce is effective and she owes the money. (3) If a husband says to his wife 'Every woman I marry, I have sold her divorce to you for a dirham' and then he marries, the wife's acceptance must occur after the marriage; before marriage it is invalid. (4) If the wife says 'I sold you my dower and ‘iddah maintenance', and the husband accepts, she is not divorced because the husband did not purchase the divorce but only the dower. The author rules that precautionary renewal of marriage is advisable. (5) The passage from al-Qunyah discusses issues without clear prior rulings. A key issue: if a wife says 'I acquit you of the dower on condition of raj‘ī divorce' and the husband pronounces a raj‘ī divorce, it actually becomes ba’in due to the exchange for money. This is similar to the issue from al-Ziyādāt. (6) Various cases from al-Dhakhīrah calculate how the money is apportioned when two divorces are pronounced, one immediate and one future. (7) The author (Ibn Nujaym) notes that he checked his copy and did not find the addition mentioned by al-Ramlī, but later found it in al-Ḥāwī. The addition discusses the principle: when both parties agree that the divorce is raj‘ī and the money is in exchange, the divorce remains raj‘ī and the husband is released from the debt. However, in the issue of al-Ziyādāt, where the woman demands two ba’in divorces for a thousand, the exchange overrides the husband's description of raj‘ī, because she did not consent to the money while the marriage continues; thus the divorces occur as ba’in. The passage ends with a note that the statement 'the one thousand is in exchange for both' contradicts another issue.

Key Terms
بائن (bā’in): An irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage.
رجعي (raj‘ī): A revocable divorce where the husband can take back the wife during the ‘iddah without a new contract.
إبراء (ibrā’): Acquittal or release from a debt or obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario from al-Qunyah, what is the ruling when a wife says 'I acquit you of the dower on condition of raj‘ī divorce' and the husband pronounces a raj‘ī divorce?
A) The divorce is raj‘ī and the husband is released
B) The divorce becomes ba’in because of the exchange
C) The divorce is invalid and the wife does not owe anything
D) The husband must pay the dower despite the acquittal

Key Takeaway
In khul‘, the exchange of money for a divorce changes the divorce to ba’in (irrevocable) even if described as raj‘ī, because the compensation necessitates termination of the marriage.

Rulings on Wording of Khul' (Four Cases)
Four distinct rulings on wording of khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling to four distinct khul' wordings and distinguish valid from invalid acceptance conditions.

Core Idea
Khul' requires offer and acceptance with specific wording; each verbal formula produces a distinct legal effect.

Khul' (divorce by redemption) is a form of bain divorce where the wife compensates the husband. The Hanafi school provides detailed rulings on the wording used by spouses. This passage presents four cases: when the wife says 'I bought', when the husband makes a conditional offer, when he refers to a future wife, and when the wife offers to sell her mahr and iddah expenses. Understanding these distinctions prevents invalid or uncertain divorces.

Guided Path
1
Analyze Case 1: Wife says 'I bought'
Identify that 'اشتريت' (I bought) is a kinayah (metaphorical expression) for accepting khul'. According to the Hanafi school, this kinayah results in a bain (irrevocable) divorce. The wife owes the agreed compensation because the husband offered khul' and she accepted using a kinayah word.
Kinayah requires intention, but here it is effective because it is in response to an offer.
2
Analyze Case 2: Husband's conditional offer with session requirement
When the husband says 'I sold your affair to you for a thousand dirhams if she chooses in the session', this is a conditional khul' offer. The condition is that the wife must choose herself (i.e., accept) during the same sitting (al-majlis). If she accepts within the session, the divorce occurs and she must pay the compensation. If she accepts outside, the offer lapses.
The session (majlis) is analogized to the option in contracts (khiyar al-majlis).
3
Analyze Case 3: Referring to a future wife
If the husband says to his current wife 'Every woman I marry, I have sold her divorce from you for a dirham', then later marries another woman, acceptance by the current wife must occur after the marriage. If she accepts before the marriage, it is invalid because the khul' is tied to the future wife's existence. The acceptance after marriage completes the khul' for that new wife (or her divorce).
This shows that khul' can be contingent on a future event, but the acceptance must follow that event.
4
Analyze Case 4: Wife selling mahr and iddah nafaqah
If the wife says 'I sell you my mahr and my iddah maintenance' and the husband says 'I bought', this transaction is a sale of property, not a khul'. The wife is not divorced because the husband did not purchase her divorce; he purchased her mahr. However, to avoid any future doubt, it is recommended (ahwat) to renew the marriage contract.
This case illustrates that the intent and wording must clearly indicate divorce; otherwise, no divorce occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منك فقالت اشتريت يقع الطلاق بائناً لأن هذا كناية وهي بائنة ولو قال لها بعت منك أمرك بألف درهم إن اختارت نفسها في المجلس وقع الطلاق ولزمها المال لأنه ملكها الطلاق بالمال، فإذا اختارت فقد تملكت ولو قال لامرأته كل امرأة أتزوجها فقد بعت طلاقها منك بدرهم ثم تزوج امرأة فالقبول إليها بعد التزوج، فإن قبلت بعد التزوج طلاقها أو طلقتها يقع، وإن قبلت قبله لا يقع لأن هذا الكلام من الزوج خلع بعد التزوج فيشترط القبول بعده. ولو قالت المرأة بعت منك مهري ونفقة عدتي فقال اشتريت فالظاهر أنها لا تطلق لأن الزوج ما باع نفسها ولا طلاقها منها إنما اشترى مهرها وهذا لا يكون طلاقاً لكن الأحوط أن يجدد النكاح ؛ كذا في المحيط .
If a woman says 'I bought' then divorce occurs as bain because this is kinayah and it is bain. And if a husband says to her 'I sold your affair to you for a thousand dirhams if she chooses herself in the session', the divorce occurs and the money is obligatory because he made her own the divorce for money; so when she chooses, she has owned it. And if a husband says to his wife 'every woman I marry, I have sold her divorce from you for a dirham', then marries a woman, acceptance belongs to her after marriage; if she accepts after marriage, her divorce or the divorce of the wife [the new wife] occurs, and if she accepts before it, it does not occur because this speech from the husband is khul' after marriage, so acceptance after it is required. And if the woman says 'I sell you my mahr and the nafaqah of my iddah' and he says 'I bought', the apparent is that she is not divorced because the husband did not sell herself nor her divorce from her; he only bought her mahr, and this is not being a divorce, but it is cautious to renew the marriage; thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage presents four distinct rulings from the Hanafi school regarding the wording of khul'. The first ruling: if the wife says 'I bought' (اشتريت) as a response to the husband's offer, this is a kinayah (metaphorical expression) for accepting the khul', and the divorce is bain (irrevocable). The second ruling: if the husband says 'I sold your affair to you for a thousand dirhams if she chooses in the session,' this is a conditional offer; if the wife chooses herself during the same session, the divorce occurs and she owes the money. The third ruling: if the husband tells his current wife that every future wife he marries is 'sold' to her for a dirham, then later marries a woman, the current wife's acceptance is required after the marriage; acceptance before the marriage is invalid because the khul' is tied to the future wife. The fourth ruling: if the wife offers to sell her mahr and iddah maintenance and the husband buys, she is not divorced because the husband bought property, not divorce; however, it is recommended to renew the marriage contract to avoid doubt.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khal'): Divorce by redemption where the wife compensates the husband for her release.
كناية (kinayah): A word that implies divorce but is not explicit, requiring intention or context to effect divorce.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce; the husband cannot take back the wife without a new marriage contract.
المجلس (al-majlis): The sitting/session of the offer, a condition for option in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a woman says 'بعت منك مهري ونفقة عدتي' and the husband says 'اشتريت', what is the ruling?
A) The divorce occurs as bain and she owes nothing
B) The divorce does not occur, but it is recommended to renew the marriage
C) The divorce occurs as raj'iy and she must pay
D) The marriage is annulled automatically

Key Takeaway
Khul' requires explicit or clear metaphorical wording directed at divorce; a sale of mahr is not a divorce.

When Financial Consideration Overrides Divorce Type: The Case of Ibra' Conditioned on Raj'iy Divorce
Resolves a case where wife offers ibra conditioned on raj'iy divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife offers ibra' from mahr conditioned on a raj'iy divorce and explain why the divorce becomes bain using the principle from al-Ziyadat.

Core Idea
Financial consideration in a divorce conditioned on raj'iy turns it into ba'in irrespective of the husband's specification.

This lesson examines a specific khul' scenario from al-Qunyah where the wife releases the husband from the mahr on condition of a raj'iy (revocable) divorce. The husband pronounces a raj'iy divorce, but the Hanafi school rules it becomes ba'in (irrevocable) due to the financial consideration. We will explore the legal reasoning, which draws an analogy to مسألة الزيادات (the issue from al-Ziyadat), and understand how the school prioritizes substance over form in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wife's offer and its condition
The wife says 'أبرأتك من المهر بشرط الطلاق الرجعي' – she releases the husband from the mahr debt on condition that he gives a raj'iy divorce. Note that the condition is a شرط, and the consideration is financial (ibra').
2
Identify the husband's response
The husband says 'أنت طالق طلاقاً رجعياً' – he explicitly pronounces a raj'iy divorce. The question is whether this specification determines the type of divorce.
3
Apply the Hanafi ruling: the divorce becomes ba'in
Despite the husband's specification, the divorce is ruled bain (irrevocable) because the financial consideration (ibra' from mahr) changes the nature of the divorce, analogous to the principle in مسألة الزيادات. In that precedent, when a husband says 'You are divorced today raj'iy and tomorrow another with a thousand,' the thousand is in exchange for both divorces, and both become ba'in.
4
Understand the ratio: financial consideration overrides verbal description
The key is that when a financial consideration is present in exchange for divorce, the default rule is that the divorce becomes ba'in, because khul' is inherently ba'in. The husband's attempt to specify raj'iy is ineffective because it contradicts the implication of the consideration.
5
Note the scope and authority
This ruling is from al-Qunyah, classified as nawadir (rare transmissions) but relied upon in later fatwa. It shows the school's nuanced approach when parties combine financial and verbal elements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية في الباب المعقود للمسائل التي لم يوجد فيها رواية ولا جواب شاف للمتأخرين آخرها قالت لزوجها أبرأتك من المهر بشرط الطلاق الرجعي فقال لها أنت طالق طلاقاً رجعياً يقع بائناً للمقابلة في المال كمسألة الزيادات. أنت طالق اليوم رجعياً وغداً أخرى بألف فالألف مقابل بهما وهما بائنتان أم رجعياً وهل يبرأ الزوج لوجود الشرط صورة أو لا يبرأ اهـ.
And in al-Qunyah, in the chapter devoted to issues for which there is no narration nor a clear answer from the late scholars, at its end: she said to her husband 'I release you from the mahr on condition of raj'iy divorce' and he said to her 'You are divorced with a raj'iy divorce.' It occurs as bain because of the financial consideration, like the issue of al-Ziyadat. 'You are divorced today raj'iy and tomorrow another with a thousand' – the thousand is in exchange for both, and they are both bain, or raj'iy? And does the husband become free from debt due to the condition in form or not? End.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage from al-Qunyah addresses a specific khul' scenario where the wife initiates by saying 'I release you from the mahr on condition that you give me a raj'iy (revocable) divorce.' The husband then says 'You are divorced with a raj'iy divorce.' The ruling is that the divorce becomes bain (irrevocable) despite the husband's specification of raj'iy, because the financial consideration (the ibra from mahr) triggers the principle applied in similar cases (مسألة الزيادات) where the payment transforms the divorce into bain. The passage then poses a further hypothetical: if a husband says 'You are divorced today raj'iy and tomorrow another with a thousand,' is the thousand in exchange for both and are both bain or raj'iy? And does the husband become free from debt? The text notes that the answer is found in the original source.

Key Terms
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Release from a debt; here, the wife releases the husband from the mahr obligation.
الطلاق الرجعي (al-talaq al-raj'iy): Revocable divorce where the husband may take back the wife during iddah without new contract.
الطلاق البائن (al-talaq al-ba'in): Irrevocable divorce requiring new marriage contract.
مسألة الزيادات (mas'alat al-ziyadat): A well-known case from the Ziyadat where a condition of raj'iy is overridden by financial consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Allocation of Payment in Multiple Divorces
Rulings on allocation of payment when multiple divorces are pronounced.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for allocating a single payment when multiple divorces are pronounced, and apply it to different scenarios.

Core Idea
A single payment for multiple divorces is allocated to all divorces, unless the first is described as raj'iy or ba'in without compensation.

The passage from al-Dhakhira presents several scenarios of divorces pronounced with a single payment. The central principle is that when a husband pronounces multiple divorces and offers a payment, the payment is distributed across all divorces proportionally. However, if the first divorce is of a type that is incompatible with payment (e.g., raj'iy or ba'in where no payment is due), the payment is assigned solely to the later divorces. This lesson will guide you through these scenarios to understand the rule clearly.

Guided Path
1
Understand the baseline rule
When a husband says 'You are divorced now one, and tomorrow another with a thousand,' the payment is split equally between the two divorces, with half for the first and half for the second. However, if he remarries her before tomorrow, the second divorce revives and the remaining half is due.
The baseline is that payment is distributed unless the first divorce is described in a way that precludes payment.
2
Identify scenarios where first divorce precludes payment
If the first divorce is described as 'I own the return' (raj'iy) or 'ba'in' (irrevocable), it occurs without payment. The full payment goes to the second divorce because the first cannot be associated with payment.
Raj'iy divorces are normally without consideration; ba'in ends the marriage immediately.
3
Handle cases where both divorces are raj'iy
If both divorces are described as 'I own the return,' the payment is allocated to both, and both become ba'in. This is because the condition 'I own the return' is incompatible with payment, so the payment transforms them into ba'in divorces.
In this case, the husband loses the right to take back his wife during iddah.
4
Apply the rule to complex statements
The passage ends with a series of statements that all follow the same logic: any divorce described as raj'iy or ba'in takes no share of the payment, and the payment is allocated to the remaining divorces.
The rule is consistent across all scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة : أنت طالق الساعة واحدة وغداً أخرى بألف درهم فقبلت وقعت واحدة في الحال بنصف الألف وأخرى غداً بغير شيء، وإن تزوجها قبل مجيء الغد ثم جاء الغد تقع أخرى بخمسمائة . أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة وغداً أخرى بألف فقبلت وقعت واحدة للحال بغير شيء وفي الغد أخرى بالألف، ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم بائنة وغداً أخرى بألف وقع للحال واحدة بائنة بغير شيء وغدا أخرى بالألف. ولو قال أنت طالق واحدة وأنت طالق أخرى بألف فقبلت وقعتا بألف ولو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الزجعة وغداً أخرى أملك الرجعة بألف فقبلت انصرف البدل إليهما، وكذا لو قال أنت طالق الساعة ثلاثاً وغداً أخرى بائنة بألف وأنت طالق الساعة واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بغير شيء بالألف فالبدل ينصرف إليهما اهـ.
And in al-Dhakhira: 'You are divorced now one, and tomorrow another with a thousand dirhams' – if she accepts, one divorce occurs immediately with half a thousand, and another tomorrow with nothing; but if he marries her before the arrival of tomorrow, then tomorrow comes, another occurs with five hundred. 'You are divorced now one, I own the return, and tomorrow another with a thousand' – if she accepts, one occurs immediately with nothing, and tomorrow another with a thousand. And if he says 'You are divorced today ba'in and tomorrow another with a thousand' – one ba'in occurs immediately with nothing, and tomorrow another with a thousand. And if he says 'You are divorced one, and you are divorced another with a thousand' – if she accepts, both occur with a thousand. And if he says 'You are divorced now one, I own the return, and tomorrow another, I own the return, with a thousand' – if she accepts, the payment is allocated to both. Likewise, if he says 'You are divorced now three, and tomorrow another ba'in with a thousand, and you are divorced now one with nothing and tomorrow another with nothing with a thousand' – the payment is allocated to both. End.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhira provides detailed scenarios of multiple divorces accompanied by a single payment. The key principle is that when a payment is mentioned after two or more divorce pronouncements, it is allocated to all of them, unless the first divorce is described with a characteristic that is incompatible with payment (such as being without compensation, or being a type that cannot be associated with payment). For example, if the husband says 'You are divorced now one, and tomorrow another with a thousand,' and the wife accepts, the payment is split: half for the first (500) and the second is without compensation immediately, but if he remarries her before tomorrow, then the second becomes due with the full payment? Actually the text says: 'one occurs immediately with half a thousand, and another tomorrow with nothing; but if he marries her before the arrival of tomorrow, then tomorrow comes, another occurs with five hundred.' This means if he remarries, the second divorce is treated as a new occurrence and the remaining half is due. In contrast, if the first is described as 'I own the return' (raj'iy), then the payment is not allocated to the first because raj'iy is incompatible with immediate payment; so the first occurs free and the second takes the full payment. Similarly, if the first is described as ba'in, it occurs free and the second takes the payment. If both are described as 'I own the return', the payment is allocated to both, and both become ba'in. The passage ends by stating that this is established in al-Dhakhira.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): The consideration (payment) in a khul' transaction.
الرجعة (al-raj'ah): The husband's right to take back his wife during iddah after a raj'iy divorce.
بائنة (ba'inah): Feminine of ba'in; an irrevocable divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The payment is allocated to all divorces unless the first is of a type that is incompatible with payment.

Obligation of Payment and Validity of Ibra' in Khul'
Commentary on the ruling that money is obligatory upon the wife in khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the money is wajib upon the wife in khul' and explain why ibra' is valid consideration.

Core Idea
The wife's money becomes wajib upon acceptance; ibra' is valid because it is property.

This lesson examines the fundamental ruling that the wife must pay the agreed sum in khul' upon acceptance. The commentator explains the underlying reasoning and extends the ruling to include cases where the wife releases the husband from a debt (ibra'). Understanding this will help you distinguish valid consideration from invalid promises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is khul' (divorce initiated by the wife for compensation). The ruling is that the money becomes wajib upon the wife at the moment of acceptance.
2
Locate the reasoning (talil)
The commentator says: 'because he (the husband) did not consent to the release of some (i.e., the marital bond) from his ownership except with it.' This means the husband's consent to divorce is contingent on receiving compensation, so the money becomes binding once she accepts.
3
Understand the author’s suggested improvement
The commentator notes that the author could have said 'the named one is for him' to also cover cases where a third party accepts on behalf of the wife (khul' al-fuduli) and to explicitly include ibra' as consideration.
4
Analyze the inclusion of ibra'
Ibra' (release from a debt) is considered property (mal) in the Hanafi school, so when a wife offers to release the husband from a debt in exchange for divorce, it is valid and the divorce becomes ba'in.
5
Note the practical consequence
When ibra' is used as consideration, the divorce is irrevocable (ba'in), meaning the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولزمها المال) أي في المسألتين لأنه ما رضي بخروج بعضها عن ملكه إلا به فلزمها المال بالقبول. ولو قال وكان المسمى له لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا قبله غيرها وسيأتي آخر الباب بيان خلع الفضولي إن شاء الله وليشمل الابراء حتى لو قالت له أبرأتك عما لي عليك على طلاقي ففعل جازت البراءة وكان الطلاق بائناً، وكذا لو طلقها على أن تبرئه من الألف التي كفل بها للمرأة . فلان من والطلاق بائن كما في البزازية. وقيد به احترازاً عن التأخير فإنه ليس بمال وأنما تتأخر فيه المطالبة كما لو قالت له طلقني على أن أؤخر مالي عليك فطلقها، فإن كان للتأخير غاية معلومة صح التأخير، وإن يكن له غاية معلومة لا يصح والطلاق رجعي على كل حال كما في البزازية أيضاً. ولو قال قد خلعتك على ألف قال ثلاث مرات فقبلت طلقت ثلاثاً بثلاثة آلاف لأنه لم يقع شيء إلا بقبولها
His statement: 'And he obligated the money to her' – i.e., in the two issues, because he did not consent to the release of some [part] from his ownership except with it, so the money is obligatory upon her with acceptance. And if he said 'and the named one is for him', it would be better to include when someone other than her accepts, and it will come at the end of the chapter the explanation of the khul' of the unauthorized person, God willing, and to include the ibra' (release). So that even if she says to him 'I release you from what is due to me upon the condition of my divorce', and he does so, the release is valid and the divorce is ba'in. Likewise, if he divorces her on the condition that she release him from the thousand which he guaranteed for the woman... [؟] and the divorce is ba'in as in al-Bazzaziyyah. He restricted it to distinguish from deferment, for it is not property; rather, only the claim is deferred. As if she says to him 'Divorce me on the condition that I defer my right upon you' and he divorces her; if the deferment has a known term, the deferment is valid; if it has no known term, it is not valid, and the divorce is raj'iy in all cases as in al-Bazzaziyyah also. And if he says 'I have divorced you in khul' for a thousand' three times, and she accepts, she is divorced three times for three thousand, because nothing occurs except with her acceptance.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the statement 'ولزمها المال' (and the money is obligatory upon her). The commentator explains that the wife owes the money because the husband did not consent to losing any part of his marital rights (including the right to the woman herself) without receiving compensation; thus, upon her acceptance, the money becomes binding. The commentator also suggests that the author's wording could be improved to include cases where someone other than the wife accepts (like a third party), and to explicitly include ibra' (release) as valid consideration. The passage then clarifies that 'money' in this context excludes mere deferment of debt, because deferment is not property but merely postponing a claim. If the wife offers to defer her existing right (like deferred mahr) and the husband divorces her, the ruling depends on whether the deferment has a known term; if it does, it is valid and the divorce is ba'in? Actually, the text says: if the deferment has a known term, it is valid; if not, it is invalid, and the divorce is raj'iy in all cases (i.e., regardless of the validity of the deferment condition, the divorce is raj'iy because the condition is not a valid consideration for khul'). The passage ends with a ruling: if the husband says 'I have divorced you in khul' for a thousand' three times and the wife accepts, she is divorced three times with three thousand due, because each pronouncement is a separate offer that takes effect upon acceptance.

Key Terms
التأخير (al-ta'khir): Deferment of payment; postponing a due right to a future date.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Release from a debt; valid as consideration in khul'.
خلع الفضولي (khal' al-fuduli): Khul' performed by an unauthorized third party (e.g., someone else accepting on behalf of the wife).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the money become wajib upon the wife in khul'?
A) Because the husband has a right to keep the wife regardless
B) Because the husband does not consent to lose his marital rights without compensation
C) Because the wife is required to pay for the divorce in all cases
D) Because the husband can demand any amount he wishes

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khul' renders the wife's payment wajib upon her acceptance, and ibra' (release from debt) is valid consideration because it is a form of property.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Deferment as Invalid Consideration in Khul'
Ruling on deferment as consideration in khul' and its effect on the type of divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid consideration in khul' by applying the rule that deferment is not property.

Core Idea
Deferment (ta'khir) is not property; if used as consideration, the divorce is raj'iy, not ba'in.

This lesson focuses on the ruling when a wife offers to defer an existing debt in exchange for khul'. The Hanafi school strictly distinguishes between actual property (like payment or ibra') and mere deferment of a claim. You will learn the conditions under which deferment might be valid and the consequences when it is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the consideration offered
The wife offers to defer (postpone) a debt that the husband owes her. This is not a transfer of property but a delay in claiming it.
2
Classify deferment in Hanafi usul
Deferment is not considered mal (property) because it does not involve the transfer of a tangible or financial right; it merely alters the time of payment.
Contrast this with ibra' which is a release and thus a transfer.
3
Apply the ruling based on conditions
If the deferment has a known (fixed) term, it is valid as a condition – the husband must wait until that time to demand the debt. If no known term, the deferment is invalid (batil).
4
Determine the type of divorce
Regardless of the validity of the deferment condition, the divorce remains raj'iy (revocable) because the consideration was not valid property. The divorce does not become ba'in even if the deferment is upheld.
This is a key distinction: invalid consideration leads to raj'iy divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولزمها المال) أي في المسألتين لأنه ما رضي بخروج بعضها عن ملكه إلا به فلزمها المال بالقبول. ولو قال وكان المسمى له لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا قبله غيرها وسيأتي آخر الباب بيان خلع الفضولي إن شاء الله وليشمل الابراء حتى لو قالت له أبرأتك عما لي عليك على طلاقي ففعل جازت البراءة وكان الطلاق بائناً، وكذا لو طلقها على أن تبرئه من الألف التي كفل بها للمرأة . فلان من والطلاق بائن كما في البزازية. وقيد به احترازاً عن التأخير فإنه ليس بمال وأنما تتأخر فيه المطالبة كما لو قالت له طلقني على أن أؤخر مالي عليك فطلقها، فإن كان للتأخير غاية معلومة صح التأخير، وإن يكن له غاية معلومة لا يصح والطلاق رجعي على كل حال كما في البزازية أيضاً. ولو قال قد خلعتك على ألف قال ثلاث مرات فقبلت طلقت ثلاثاً بثلاثة آلاف لأنه لم يقع شيء إلا بقبولها
His statement: 'And he obligated the money to her' – i.e., in the two issues, because he did not consent to the release of some [part] from his ownership except with it, so the money is obligatory upon her with acceptance. And if he said 'and the named one is for him', it would be better to include when someone other than her accepts, and it will come at the end of the chapter the explanation of the khul' of the unauthorized person, God willing, and to include the ibra' (release). So that even if she says to him 'I release you from what is due to me upon the condition of my divorce', and he does so, the release is valid and the divorce is ba'in. Likewise, if he divorces her on the condition that she release him from the thousand which he guaranteed for the woman... [؟] and the divorce is ba'in as in al-Bazzaziyyah. He restricted it to distinguish from deferment, for it is not property; rather, only the claim is deferred. As if she says to him 'Divorce me on the condition that I defer my right upon you' and he divorces her; if the deferment has a known term, the deferment is valid; if it has no known term, it is not valid, and the divorce is raj'iy in all cases as in al-Bazzaziyyah also. And if he says 'I have divorced you in khul' for a thousand' three times, and she accepts, she is divorced three times for three thousand, because nothing occurs except with her acceptance.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the statement 'ولزمها المال' (and the money is obligatory upon her). The commentator explains that the wife owes the money because the husband did not consent to losing any part of his marital rights (including the right to the woman herself) without receiving compensation; thus, upon her acceptance, the money becomes binding. The commentator also suggests that the author's wording could be improved to include cases where someone other than the wife accepts (like a third party), and to explicitly include ibra' (release) as valid consideration. The passage then clarifies that 'money' in this context excludes mere deferment of debt, because deferment is not property but merely postponing a claim. If the wife offers to defer her existing right (like deferred mahr) and the husband divorces her, the ruling depends on whether the deferment has a known term; if it does, it is valid and the divorce is ba'in? Actually, the text says: if the deferment has a known term, it is valid; if not, it is invalid, and the divorce is raj'iy in all cases (i.e., regardless of the validity of the deferment condition, the divorce is raj'iy because the condition is not a valid consideration for khul'). The passage ends with a ruling: if the husband says 'I have divorced you in khul' for a thousand' three times and the wife accepts, she is divorced three times with three thousand due, because each pronouncement is a separate offer that takes effect upon acceptance.

Key Terms
التأخير (al-ta'khir): Deferment of payment; postponing a due right to a future date.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the divorce if the wife offers to defer a debt without a known term?
A) The deferment is invalid and the divorce is ba'in
B) The deferment is invalid and the divorce is raj'iy
C) The deferment is valid and the divorce is raj'iy
D) The deferment is valid and the divorce is ba'in

Key Takeaway
Deferment (ta'khir) is not property; even if valid as a condition with a known term, the divorce in khul' remains raj'iy, not ba'in.

Effect of Repeating the Khul' Offer Three Times
Ruling on the effect of repeating the khul' offer and acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a husband repeats the khul' offer three times and the wife accepts.

Core Idea
Each pronouncement of khul' is a separate offer; three acceptances equal three divorces and three separate payments.

This brief lesson addresses a scenario where the husband says 'I have divorced you in khul' for a thousand' three times, and the wife accepts after each. The commentator explains that because nothing occurs except with acceptance, each pronouncement results in a separate divorce with a separate thousand due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the number of offers
The husband repeats the offer three times: 'I have divorced you in khul' for a thousand' said three times.
2
Apply the principle of acceptance
Each pronouncement is a new offer. Nothing happens until acceptance. The wife accepts each offer, either simultaneously or sequentially. Since each offer is separate, each acceptance triggers a separate khul' contract.
3
Determine the total amount
Because three separate khul' contracts are formed, the wife owes three thousand (1,000 each).
4
Count the divorces
Each khul' results in one ba'in divorce. Since khul' divorces are ba'in, three such divorces amount to three separate irrevocable divorces. The wife becomes completely forbidden to the husband (if she has not already been divorced three times).
The text says 'she is divorced three times' – meaning three ba'in divorces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولزمها المال) أي في المسألتين لأنه ما رضي بخروج بعضها عن ملكه إلا به فلزمها المال بالقبول. ولو قال وكان المسمى له لكان أولى ليشمل ما إذا قبله غيرها وسيأتي آخر الباب بيان خلع الفضولي إن شاء الله وليشمل الابراء حتى لو قالت له أبرأتك عما لي عليك على طلاقي ففعل جازت البراءة وكان الطلاق بائناً، وكذا لو طلقها على أن تبرئه من الألف التي كفل بها للمرأة . فلان من والطلاق بائن كما في البزازية. وقيد به احترازاً عن التأخير فإنه ليس بمال وأنما تتأخر فيه المطالبة كما لو قالت له طلقني على أن أؤخر مالي عليك فطلقها، فإن كان للتأخير غاية معلومة صح التأخير، وإن يكن له غاية معلومة لا يصح والطلاق رجعي على كل حال كما في البزازية أيضاً. ولو قال قد خلعتك على ألف قال ثلاث مرات فقبلت طلقت ثلاثاً بثلاثة آلاف لأنه لم يقع شيء إلا بقبولها
His statement: 'And he obligated the money to her' – i.e., in the two issues, because he did not consent to the release of some [part] from his ownership except with it, so the money is obligatory upon her with acceptance. And if he said 'and the named one is for him', it would be better to include when someone other than her accepts, and it will come at the end of the chapter the explanation of the khul' of the unauthorized person, God willing, and to include the ibra' (release). So that even if she says to him 'I release you from what is due to me upon the condition of my divorce', and he does so, the release is valid and the divorce is ba'in. Likewise, if he divorces her on the condition that she release him from the thousand which he guaranteed for the woman... [؟] and the divorce is ba'in as in al-Bazzaziyyah. He restricted it to distinguish from deferment, for it is not property; rather, only the claim is deferred. And if he says 'I have divorced you in khul' for a thousand' three times, and she accepts, she is divorced three times for three thousand, because nothing occurs except with her acceptance.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the statement 'ولزمها المال' (and the money is obligatory upon her). The commentator explains that the wife owes the money because the husband did not consent to losing any part of his marital rights (including the right to the woman herself) without receiving compensation; thus, upon her acceptance, the money becomes binding. The commentator also suggests that the author's wording could be improved to include cases where someone other than the wife accepts (like a third party), and to explicitly include ibra' (release) as valid consideration. The passage then clarifies that 'money' in this context excludes mere deferment of debt, because deferment is not property but merely postponing a claim. Key Terms
التأخير (al-ta'khir): Deferment of payment; postponing a due right to a future date.
الإبراء (al-ibra'): Release from a debt; valid as consideration in khul'.
خلع الفضولي (khal' al-fuduli): Khul' performed by an unauthorized third party (e.g., someone else accepting on behalf of the wife).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many divorces occur if the husband says the khul' offer three times and the wife accepts each time?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce because the offers are not separate

Key Takeaway
Repeating the khul' offer with separate acceptances results in multiple independent khul' contracts, each with its own payment and each causing a ba'in divorce.
